			<h1 id="firstHeading" class="firstHeading" lang="en">War of the Austrian Succession</h1>
									<div id="bodyContent" class="mw-body-content">
									<div id="siteSub" class="noprint">From Wikipedia, the free encyclopedia</div>
								<div id="contentSub"></div>
												<div id="jump-to-nav" class="mw-jump">
					Jump to:					<a href="#mw-head">navigation</a>, 					<a href="#p-search">search</a>
				</div>
				<div id="mw-content-text" lang="en" dir="ltr" class="mw-content-ltr"><div class="mw-parser-output"><table class="mw-stack mobile-float-reset" role="presentation" style="float:right;clear:right;background:transparent;margin:0;padding:0">
<tr>
<td>
<table class="infobox vevent" style="border-spacing:2px;;width:315px">
<tr>
<th class="summary" colspan="2" style="background-color:#B0C4DE;text-align:center;vertical-align:middle;font-size:110%;">War of the Austrian Succession</th>
</tr>
<tr>
<td colspan="2" style="text-align:center;border-bottom:1px solid #aaa;line-height:1.5em;"><a href="/wiki/File:Battle_of_Fontenoy_1745.PNG" class="image"><img alt="Battle of Fontenoy 1745.PNG" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1c/Battle_of_Fontenoy_1745.PNG/300px-Battle_of_Fontenoy_1745.PNG" width="300" height="250" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1c/Battle_of_Fontenoy_1745.PNG/450px-Battle_of_Fontenoy_1745.PNG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1c/Battle_of_Fontenoy_1745.PNG/600px-Battle_of_Fontenoy_1745.PNG 2x" data-file-width="1240" data-file-height="1034" /></a><br />
<i>The <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Fontenoy" title="Battle of Fontenoy">Battle of Fontenoy</a></i> by <a href="/wiki/Pierre_L%27Enfant_(painter)" title="Pierre L'Enfant (painter)">Pierre L'Enfant</a>. Oil on canvas.</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<td colspan="2">
<table style="width:100%;margin:0;padding:0;border:0">
<tr>
<th style="padding-right:1em">Date</th>
<td>16 December 1740 – 18 October 1748<br />
(7&#160;years, 10&#160;months and 2&#160;days)</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<th style="padding-right:1em">Location</th>
<td><span class="location"><a href="/wiki/Europe" title="Europe">Europe</a>, <a href="/wiki/North_America" title="North America">North America</a> and <a href="/wiki/Indian_subcontinent" title="Indian subcontinent">India</a></span></td>
</tr>
<tr>
<th style="padding-right:1em">Result</th>
<td><a href="/wiki/Treaty_of_Aix-la-Chapelle_(1748)" title="Treaty of Aix-la-Chapelle (1748)">Treaty of Aix-la-Chapelle</a>
<div>
<div>
<ul>
<li>Maria Theresa retains the Austrian, Bohemian and Hungarian thrones</li>
<li>Francis of Lorraine, Maria Theresa's husband, confirmed as Holy Roman Emperor</li>
</ul>
</div>
</div>
</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<th style="padding-right:1em">Territorial<br />
changes</th>
<td>
<div class="plainlist">
<ul>
<li>Prussian control of <a href="/wiki/Silesia" title="Silesia">Silesia</a> confirmed.</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Duchy_of_Parma" title="Duchy of Parma">Duchies of Parma</a>, <a href="/wiki/Piacenza" title="Piacenza">Piacenza</a> and <a href="/wiki/Duchy_of_Guastalla" title="Duchy of Guastalla">Guastalla</a> restored to the <a href="/wiki/House_of_Bourbon-Parma" title="House of Bourbon-Parma">Spanish Bourbons</a>.</li>
<li>France gains the Austrian Netherlands but returns them to Austria.</li>
</ul>
</div>
</td>
</tr>
</table>
</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<th colspan="2" style="background-color:#B0C4DE;text-align:center;vertical-align:middle;font-size:110%;">Belligerents</th>

<th colspan="2" style="background-color:#B0C4DE;text-align:center;vertical-align:middle;font-size:110%;">Commanders and leaders</th>
</tr>
<tr>
<td style="width:50%;border-right:1px dotted #aaa;">

</table>
<p>The <b>War of the Austrian Succession</b> (<a href="/wiki/German_language" title="German language">German</a>: <span lang="de" xml:lang="de"><i>Österreichischer Erbfolgekrieg</i></span>, 1740–48) involved most of the <a href="/wiki/Power_in_international_relations" class="mw-redirect" title="Power in international relations">powers</a> of <a href="/wiki/Europe" title="Europe">Europe</a> over the question of <a href="/wiki/Maria_Theresa" title="Maria Theresa">Maria Theresa</a>'s succession to the <a href="/wiki/Habsburg_Monarchy" title="Habsburg Monarchy">Habsburg Monarchy</a>. The war included <a href="/wiki/King_George%27s_War" title="King George's War">King George's War</a> in <a href="/wiki/British_America" title="British America">British America</a>, the <a href="/wiki/War_of_Jenkins%27_Ear" title="War of Jenkins' Ear">War of Jenkins' Ear</a> (which formally began on 23 October 1739), the <a href="/wiki/First_Carnatic_War" title="First Carnatic War">First Carnatic War</a> in <a href="/wiki/Nizam_of_Hyderabad" title="Nizam of Hyderabad">India</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Jacobite_rising_of_1745" title="Jacobite rising of 1745">Jacobite rising of 1745</a> in <a href="/wiki/Scotland" title="Scotland">Scotland</a>, and the <a href="/wiki/First_Silesian_War" title="First Silesian War">First</a> and <a href="/wiki/Second_Silesian_War" class="mw-redirect" title="Second Silesian War">Second Silesian Wars</a>.</p>
<p>The war began under the pretext that Maria Theresa was ineligible to succeed to the Habsburg thrones of her father, <a href="/wiki/Charles_VI,_Holy_Roman_Emperor" title="Charles VI, Holy Roman Emperor">Charles VI</a>, because <a href="/wiki/Salic_law" title="Salic law">Salic law</a> precluded royal inheritance by a woman. In practice, the challenge of eligibility was an excuse put forward by <a href="/wiki/Kingdom_of_Prussia" title="Kingdom of Prussia">Prussia</a> and France to challenge Habsburg power. Austria was supported by <a href="/wiki/Kingdom_of_Great_Britain" title="Kingdom of Great Britain">Great Britain</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Dutch_Republic" title="Dutch Republic">Dutch Republic</a>, the traditional enemies of France, as well as the <a href="/wiki/Kingdom_of_Sardinia" title="Kingdom of Sardinia">Kingdom of Sardinia</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Electorate_of_Saxony" title="Electorate of Saxony">Electorate of Saxony</a>. France and Prussia were allied with the <a href="/wiki/Electorate_of_Bavaria" title="Electorate of Bavaria">Electorate of Bavaria</a>.</p>
<p>Spain, which had been at war with Britain over colonies and trade ever since 1739, entered the war on the Continent to re-establish its influence in northern Italy, further reversing an Austrian dominance over the Italian peninsula that had been achieved at Spain's expense as a consequence of Spain's <a href="/wiki/War_of_the_Spanish_Succession" title="War of the Spanish Succession">war of succession</a> earlier in the 18th century.</p>
<p>The war ended with the <a href="/wiki/Treaty_of_Aix-la-Chapelle_(1748)" title="Treaty of Aix-la-Chapelle (1748)">Treaty of Aix-la-Chapelle</a> in 1748, by which Maria Theresa was confirmed as Archduchess of Austria and Queen of Hungary, but Prussia retained control of <a href="/wiki/Silesia" title="Silesia">Silesia</a>. But the peace was soon to be shattered, when Austria's desire to recapture Silesia intertwined with the <a href="/wiki/Diplomatic_Revolution" title="Diplomatic Revolution">great political changes in Europe</a>, which ended up with <a href="/wiki/Seven_Years%27_War" title="Seven Years' War">the Seven Years' War</a>.</p>
<p></p>

<p></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Background">Background</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=War_of_the_Austrian_Succession&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: Background">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Europe_1740_en.png" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/11/Europe_1740_en.png/220px-Europe_1740_en.png" width="220" height="157" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/11/Europe_1740_en.png/330px-Europe_1740_en.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/11/Europe_1740_en.png/440px-Europe_1740_en.png 2x" data-file-width="3872" data-file-height="2761" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Europe_1740_en.png" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Europe in the years after the <a href="/wiki/Treaty_of_Vienna_(1738)" title="Treaty of Vienna (1738)">Treaty of Vienna (1738)</a>, with the Habsburg Monarchy in gold</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>The immediate cause of the War of the Austrian Succession was the death in 1740 of the Holy Roman Emperor, <a href="/wiki/Charles_VI,_Holy_Roman_Emperor" title="Charles VI, Holy Roman Emperor">Charles VI</a> and his daughter <a href="/wiki/Maria_Theresa" title="Maria Theresa">Maria Theresa's</a> inheritance of Hapsburg territories in Austria, Hungary, Croatia, the Austrian Netherlands, Bohemia and Italy (often collectively referred to as 'Austria' or 'Hapsburg'). However, the war was only partially about dynastic rights; the various legal claims were largely pretexts, the real issues territorial ambitions and the balance of power.<sup id="cite_ref-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-1">[1]</a></sup></p>
<p>The underlying problem was that <a href="/wiki/Salic_law" title="Salic law">Salic law</a> prevented women inheriting the Hapsburg possessions but when his elder brother <a href="/wiki/Joseph_I,_Holy_Roman_Emperor" title="Joseph I, Holy Roman Emperor">Joseph I</a> died in 1711, Charles was the last male heir in the direct line. The 1713 <a href="/wiki/Pragmatic_Sanction_of_1713" title="Pragmatic Sanction of 1713">Pragmatic Sanction</a> ensured the integrity of the Hapsburg dominions by allowing a female successor and between 1720-1735, it was approved by the various Hapsburg territories, <a href="/wiki/Imperial_Diet_(Holy_Roman_Empire)" title="Imperial Diet (Holy Roman Empire)">the Imperial Diet</a> as well as Spain, Russia, Prussia, Britain and France.<sup id="cite_ref-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-2">[2]</a></sup> The position of Holy Roman Emperor itself was entirely separate, elective and not open to women; although far less powerful than in the past, the title conferred great prestige and who would follow Charles was also an open question.</p>
<p>The Hapsburg succession became a wider issue because Maria Theresa's birth in 1717 disinherited Joseph's daughters and Charles' nieces, <a href="/wiki/Maria_Josepha_of_Austria" title="Maria Josepha of Austria">Maria Josepha</a> and <a href="/wiki/Maria_Amalia_of_Austria" title="Maria Amalia of Austria">Maria Amalia</a>, married respectively to the rulers of Bavaria and Saxony. Both states refused to acquiesce in the Imperial Diet's decision and in 1738, Bavaria signed a secret treaty with its long-time ally France; despite accepting the Pragmatic Sanction in 1735, France now also promised to back the 'just claims' of <a href="/wiki/Charles_VII,_Holy_Roman_Emperor" title="Charles VII, Holy Roman Emperor">Charles Albert of Bavaria</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-3">[3]</a></sup> To bolster support for Maria Theresa, Charles backed <a href="/wiki/Augustus_III_of_Poland" title="Augustus III of Poland">Augustus, Elector of Saxony</a> in the 1733-35 <a href="/wiki/War_of_the_Polish_Succession" title="War of the Polish Succession">War of the Polish Succession</a> and Russia in the <a href="/wiki/Russo-Turkish_War_(1735%E2%80%931739)" title="Russo-Turkish War (1735–1739)">Russo-Turkish War of 1735–1739</a>. Their disastrous losses of men, money and territory in essentially pointless conflicts (most of the actual fighting in the War of the Polish Succession took place in Italy) substantially weakened Austria at exactly the wrong time; many diplomats and Austrian statesmen were sceptical it could survive Charles' death, which finally occurred in October 1740.<sup id="cite_ref-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-4">[4]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Strategies">Strategies</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=War_of_the_Austrian_Succession&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: Strategies">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:302px;"><a href="/wiki/File:WaroftheAustrianSuccession.png" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/97/WaroftheAustrianSuccession.png/300px-WaroftheAustrianSuccession.png" width="300" height="139" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/97/WaroftheAustrianSuccession.png/450px-WaroftheAustrianSuccession.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/97/WaroftheAustrianSuccession.png/600px-WaroftheAustrianSuccession.png 2x" data-file-width="1357" data-file-height="628" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:WaroftheAustrianSuccession.png" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
All the participants of the War of the Austrian Succession. <span style="color:Blue;">Blue</span>: Austria, Great Britain, the <a href="/wiki/Dutch_Republic" title="Dutch Republic">United Provinces</a> with allies. <span style="color:Green;">Green</span>: Prussia, Spain, France with allies.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>For much of the eighteenth century, France approached its wars in the same way. It would let its colonies defend themselves, or would offer only minimal help (sending them only limited numbers of troops or inexperienced soldiers), anticipating that fights for the colonies would likely be lost anyway.<sup id="cite_ref-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-5">[5]</a></sup> This strategy was, to a degree, forced upon France: geography, coupled with the superiority of the British navy, made it difficult for the French navy to provide significant supplies and support to French colonies.<sup id="cite_ref-6" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-6">[6]</a></sup> Similarly, several long land borders made an effective domestic army imperative for any ruler of France.<sup id="cite_ref-borneman_7-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-borneman-7">[7]</a></sup> Given these military necessities, the French government, unsurprisingly, based its strategy overwhelmingly on the army in Europe: it would keep most of its army on the European continent, hoping that such a force would be victorious closer to home.<sup id="cite_ref-borneman_7-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-borneman-7">[7]</a></sup> At the end of the war, France gave back its European conquests, and recovered such lost overseas possessions as <a href="/wiki/Fortress_of_Louisbourg" title="Fortress of Louisbourg">Louisbourg</a>, largely restoring the <i>status quo ante</i> as far as France was concerned.<sup id="cite_ref-8" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-8">[8]</a></sup></p>
<p>The British—by inclination as well as for pragmatic reasons—had tended to avoid large-scale commitments of troops on the Continent.<sup id="cite_ref-9" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-9">[9]</a></sup> They sought to offset the disadvantage this created in Europe by allying themselves with one or more Continental powers whose interests were antithetical to those of their enemies, particularly France. For the War of the Austrian Succession, the British were allied with Austria; by the time of the <a href="/wiki/Seven_Years%27_War" title="Seven Years' War">Seven Years' War</a>, they were allied with its enemy, <a href="/wiki/Prussia" title="Prussia">Prussia</a>. In marked contrast to France, Britain strove to actively prosecute the war in the colonies once it became involved in the war, taking full advantage of its <a href="/wiki/Naval_power" class="mw-redirect" title="Naval power">naval power</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-black_10-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-black-10">[10]</a></sup> The British pursued a dual strategy of <a href="/wiki/Naval_blockade" class="mw-redirect" title="Naval blockade">naval blockade</a> and bombardment of enemy ports, and also utilized their ability to move troops by sea to the utmost.<sup id="cite_ref-11" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-11">[11]</a></sup> They would harass enemy shipping and attack enemy outposts, frequently using colonists from nearby British colonies in the effort. This plan worked better in North America than in Europe, but set the stage for the Seven Years' War.</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Silesian_Campaign_of_1740">Silesian Campaign of 1740</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=War_of_the_Austrian_Succession&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: Silesian Campaign of 1740">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Maria_Theresia_of_Austria_001.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/30/Maria_Theresia_of_Austria_001.jpg/220px-Maria_Theresia_of_Austria_001.jpg" width="220" height="309" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/30/Maria_Theresia_of_Austria_001.jpg/330px-Maria_Theresia_of_Austria_001.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/30/Maria_Theresia_of_Austria_001.jpg/440px-Maria_Theresia_of_Austria_001.jpg 2x" data-file-width="546" data-file-height="768" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Maria_Theresia_of_Austria_001.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
<a href="/wiki/Maria_Theresa" title="Maria Theresa">Maria Theresa</a>, Queen regnant of Hungary and Bohemia and Archduchess of Austria, Holy Roman Empress</div>
</div>
</div>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Further information: <a href="/wiki/First_Silesian_War" title="First Silesian War">First Silesian War</a></div>
<p>Prussia in 1740 was an <a href="/wiki/Power_(international_relations)" title="Power (international relations)">emerging power</a>, a small but well-organized state whose new king, <a href="/wiki/Frederick_II_of_Prussia" class="mw-redirect" title="Frederick II of Prussia">Frederick II</a> wanted to unify the disparate and scattered holdings of his crown by gathering intervening lands into a unified, contiguous state. Prince Frederick had been only 28 years of age on 31 May 1740 when his father, <a href="/wiki/Frederick_William_I_of_Prussia" title="Frederick William I of Prussia">Frederick William I</a> died and Prince Frederick ascended to the throne.<sup id="cite_ref-Luvaas.2C_p._3_12-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Luvaas.2C_p._3-12">[12]</a></sup> Although Prussia and Austria had been allies in the <a href="/wiki/War_of_the_Polish_Succession" title="War of the Polish Succession">War of the Polish Succession</a> (1733–1738), concluded only two years before, the interests of the two countries diverged when the Holy Roman Emperor, Charles VI, died on 20 October 1740. Neither Frederick nor his father had ever been fond of Austria and its various snubs against Prussia (such as offering them the duchies of Julich and Berg in return for an alliance, only to renege later).<sup id="cite_ref-Clark_13-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Clark-13">[13]</a></sup></p>
<p>Emperor Charles VI had made provision for the succession of his daughter, <a href="/wiki/Maria_Theresa" title="Maria Theresa">Maria Theresa</a> to the throne as Empress of the Holy Roman Empire. Although the <a href="/wiki/Salic_law" title="Salic law">Salic law</a> prevented succession through the female line, during his lifetime Emperor Charles VI obtained consent from several of the individual German states that were a part of the Holy Roman Empire for his <a href="/wiki/Pragmatic_Sanction_of_1713" title="Pragmatic Sanction of 1713">Pragmatic Sanction of 1713</a> which circumvented the Salic Law to allow his daughter to succeed to the throne.<sup id="cite_ref-14" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-14">[14]</a></sup> While the Austrian Habsburg Monarchy was distracted by the succession, Frederick, upon coming to the throne, rejected the Pragmatic Sanction of 1713 and opportunistically invaded Silesia on 16 December 1740.<sup id="cite_ref-15" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-15">[15]</a></sup> In support of his invasion of Silesia, Frederick also used a questionable interpretation of a treaty (1537) between the Hohenzollerns and the Piasts of Brieg as pretext. What Frederick really feared was that other princes of Europe were preparing to exploit the succession struggle to acquire Habsburg possessions for themselves and/or diminish the power of the Holy Roman Empire. In particular, Frederick feared that <a href="/wiki/Augustus_III_of_Poland" title="Augustus III of Poland">Augustus III</a>, Elector of Saxony and King of Poland, was preparing to seize Silesia for himself to unite Saxony and Poland.<sup id="cite_ref-16" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-16">[16]</a></sup></p>
<p>The only recent combat experience of the Prussian Army was their participation in the <a href="/wiki/War_of_the_Polish_Succession" title="War of the Polish Succession">War of the Polish Succession</a> (<i>Rhine campaign of 1733–1735</i>), in which the Prussians had largely been kept out of combat. Nobody in the court of the Holy Roman Empire trusted the motives of the new rising power of Prussia and, therefore<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (October 2015)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup>, the Holy Roman Emperor did not call on the Prussians, who were vassals<sup class="noprint Inline-Template" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Accuracy_dispute#Disputed_statement" title="Wikipedia:Accuracy dispute"><span title="The material near this tag is possibly inaccurate or nonfactual. (October 2015)">dubious</span></a> <span class="metadata">– <a href="/wiki/Talk:War_of_the_Austrian_Succession#Dubious" title="Talk:War of the Austrian Succession">discuss</a></span></i>]</sup> of the Holy Roman Empire, for military support of the Empire. Accordingly, the Prussian Army had an uninspiring reputation and was counted as one of the many minor armies of the Holy Roman Empire. This reputation misrepresented the fact of a standing army of 80,000 soldiers, representing 4% of the 2.2 million population of Prussia.<sup id="cite_ref-17" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-17">[17]</a></sup> Thus the Prussian Army was disproportionate to the size of the state it protected. By comparison, the Austrian Empire had 16 million citizens but had an army only half its authorised size because of financial restraints. Thus, in defending the vast territory of the Austrian Empire this small army was more of "a sieve"<sup id="cite_ref-18" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-18">[18]</a></sup> than a shield against foreign invasion.</p>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Crown_of_Bohemia_1648.png" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/03/Crown_of_Bohemia_1648.png/220px-Crown_of_Bohemia_1648.png" width="220" height="210" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/03/Crown_of_Bohemia_1648.png/330px-Crown_of_Bohemia_1648.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/03/Crown_of_Bohemia_1648.png/440px-Crown_of_Bohemia_1648.png 2x" data-file-width="1134" data-file-height="1084" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Crown_of_Bohemia_1648.png" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
<a href="/wiki/Lands_of_the_Bohemian_Crown" title="Lands of the Bohemian Crown">Lands of the Bohemian Crown</a> until 1742 when most of <a href="/wiki/Silesia" title="Silesia">Silesia</a> was <a href="/wiki/Treaty_of_Berlin_(1742)" title="Treaty of Berlin (1742)">ceded</a> to Prussia</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Moreover, the Prussian army was better trained than other armies in Europe and was led by an excellent officer corps. King <a href="/wiki/Frederick_William_I_of_Prussia" title="Frederick William I of Prussia">Frederick William I</a> and "the guiding genius of the Prussian Army",<sup id="cite_ref-19" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-19">[19]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Leopold_I,_Prince_of_Anhalt-Dessau" title="Leopold I, Prince of Anhalt-Dessau">Leopold I, Prince of Anhalt-Dessau</a> or "Old Dessauer", had drilled the Prussian Army to a perfection previously unknown in Europe. The Prussian <a href="/wiki/Infantry" title="Infantry">infantry</a> soldier was so well-trained and well-equipped that he could fire 5 shots a minute to an Austrian's 3 shots per minute; and while Prussian <a href="/wiki/Cavalry" title="Cavalry">cavalry</a> and <a href="/wiki/Artillery" title="Artillery">artillery</a> were comparatively less efficient, they were still of better quality than average. Furthermore, while the Austrians had to wait for conscription to complete the field forces, Prussian regiments took the field at once. With this army it might not have been surprising that Frederick was able to overrun Silesia. However, Frederick sought even more advantages in the war he was planning. Accordingly, he had his Foreign Minister—<a href="/w/index.php?title=Heinrich_von_Podewils&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Heinrich von Podewils (page does not exist)">Heinrich von Podewils</a>—secretly negotiate a treaty with France to put Austria in a two front war. In this way, Prussia could attack the Austrians in the east while France would attack Austria from the west. A treaty with France was signed in April 1739.<sup id="cite_ref-20" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-20">[20]</a></sup></p>
<p>In early December, Frederick assembled his army along the <a href="/wiki/Oder" title="Oder">Oder</a> river and on 16th December, without a formal declaration of war, the Prussians invaded Silesia. For most of the previous century, Austria's military resources had been concentrated in Hungary and Italy, countering threats from the Ottomans and Spanish respectively, while neglecting less vulnerable areas. As a result, the Austrians had less than 3,000 troops available to defend Silesia and although this was increased to 7,000 shortly before the Prussian attack, they could only hold the fortresses of <a href="/wiki/Glogau" class="mw-redirect" title="Glogau">Glogau</a>, <a href="/wiki/Breslau" class="mw-redirect" title="Breslau">Breslau</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Brzeg" title="Brzeg">Brieg</a>, abandoning the rest of the province and retreating into Moravia, at which point both sides went into winter quarters. <sup id="cite_ref-21" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-21">[21]</a></sup> Prussia now controlled most of the single richest province in the Hapsburg Empire (Silesian taxes provided 10% of total Imperial income), with a population of over one million, the major commercial centre of Breslau and large mining, weaving and dyeing industries. <sup id="cite_ref-22" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-22">[22]</a></sup> However, Frederick had hoped to avoid a long war by rapidly capturing all of Silesia, presenting Maria Theresa with a fait accompli, in exchange for which Prussia would guarantee the Hapsburgs' other German territories; Austria's retention of its fortresses in Southern Silesia and the failure of Prussian diplomatic efforts to persuade powers like Britain and Russia to agree meant a quick victory could not be achieved. <sup id="cite_ref-23" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-23">[23]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Allies_in_Bohemia_1741">Allies in Bohemia 1741</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=War_of_the_Austrian_Succession&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: Allies in Bohemia 1741">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Crown_prince_Friedrich_II,_by_Antoine_Pesne.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7c/Crown_prince_Friedrich_II%2C_by_Antoine_Pesne.jpg/220px-Crown_prince_Friedrich_II%2C_by_Antoine_Pesne.jpg" width="220" height="278" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7c/Crown_prince_Friedrich_II%2C_by_Antoine_Pesne.jpg/330px-Crown_prince_Friedrich_II%2C_by_Antoine_Pesne.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7c/Crown_prince_Friedrich_II%2C_by_Antoine_Pesne.jpg/440px-Crown_prince_Friedrich_II%2C_by_Antoine_Pesne.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1468" data-file-height="1858" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Crown_prince_Friedrich_II,_by_Antoine_Pesne.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Frederick II of Prussia</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Early in the year, a new Austrian field army under general <a href="/wiki/Wilhelm_Reinhard_von_Neipperg" title="Wilhelm Reinhard von Neipperg">Wilhelm Reinhard von Neipperg</a> relieved Neisse and marched on Brieg, threatening to cut the Prussians off. On 10 April, Frederick's army caught the Austrians on the snow-covered fields near Mollwitz.<sup id="cite_ref-24" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-24">[24]</a></sup> This was the first time that Frederick had led troops into battle.<sup id="cite_ref-Jay_Luvaas_p._4_25-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Jay_Luvaas_p._4-25">[25]</a></sup> The victory that Frederick attained at the <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Mollwitz" title="Battle of Mollwitz">Battle of Mollwitz</a> was a learning experience for the young King, who departed from the field just before his troops routed the Austrians; both his tactics and his cavalry were rather clumsy, and victory was only obtained due to the discipline of the Prussian infantry and their veteran commander, Field Marshall Kurt von Schwerin.<sup id="cite_ref-26" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-26">[26]</a></sup></p>
<p>Frederick obtained an alliance with the French against the Austrians, signing the Treaty of Breslau on 5 June.<sup id="cite_ref-Robert_B._Asprey_p._181_27-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Robert_B._Asprey_p._181-27">[27]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Jeremy_Black_p._13_28-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Jeremy_Black_p._13-28">[28]</a></sup> Accordingly, the French began to cross the Rhine on 15 August<sup id="cite_ref-Jeremy_Black_p._13_28-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Jeremy_Black_p._13-28">[28]</a></sup> and joined the Bavarian Elector's forces on the <a href="/wiki/Danube" title="Danube">Danube</a> and advanced towards <a href="/wiki/Vienna" title="Vienna">Vienna</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Robert_B._Asprey_p._223_29-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Robert_B._Asprey_p._223-29">[29]</a></sup> The combined forces of the French and the Bavarians captured the Austrian town of Linz on 14 September.<sup id="cite_ref-Jeremy_Black_p._13_28-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Jeremy_Black_p._13-28">[28]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Robert_B._Asprey_p._223_29-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Robert_B._Asprey_p._223-29">[29]</a></sup> However, at this point, the objective was suddenly changed, and after many countermarches the anti-Austrian allies advanced, in three widely separated <a href="/wiki/Corps" title="Corps">corps</a>, on <a href="/wiki/Prague" title="Prague">Prague</a>. A French corps moved via <a href="/wiki/Amberg" title="Amberg">Amberg</a> and <a href="/wiki/Plze%C5%88" title="Plzeň">Pilsen</a>. The Elector marched on <a href="/wiki/Budweis" class="mw-redirect" title="Budweis">Budweis</a>, and the Saxons (who had now joined the allies against Austria<sup id="cite_ref-Robert_B._Asprey_p._223_29-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Robert_B._Asprey_p._223-29">[29]</a></sup>) invaded <a href="/wiki/Bohemia" title="Bohemia">Bohemia</a> by the <a href="/wiki/Elbe" title="Elbe">Elbe</a> valley. The Austrians could at first offer little resistance, but before long a considerable force intervened at <a href="/wiki/T%C3%A1bor" title="Tábor">Tábor</a> between the Danube and the allies, and Austrian troops including Neipperg were soon transferred from Silesia back to the west to defend the Austrian capital, Vienna, from the French.</p>
<p>With fewer Austrian troops in Silesia Frederick now had an easier time. The remaining fortresses in Silesia were taken by the Prussians.<sup id="cite_ref-Robert_B._Asprey_p._181_27-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Robert_B._Asprey_p._181-27">[27]</a></sup> Before he left Silesia, Austrian General Neipperg had made a curious agreement with Frederick, the so-called Klein-Schnellendorf agreement (9 October 1741). By this agreement, the fortress at Neisse was surrendered after a mock siege, and the Prussians agreed to let the Austrians leave unmolested releasing Neipperg's army for service elsewhere.<sup id="cite_ref-30" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-30">[30]</a></sup> At the same time the <a href="/wiki/Hungary" title="Hungary">Hungarians</a>, moved to enthusiasm by the personal appeal, in September 1741, of Maria Theresia,<sup id="cite_ref-31" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-31">[31]</a></sup> had put into the field a <i>levée en masse,</i> or "insurrection," which furnished the regular army with an invaluable force of 60,000 more light troops.<sup id="cite_ref-Asprey-p290_32-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Asprey-p290-32">[32]</a></sup> A fresh army was collected under Field Marshal <a href="/wiki/Ludwig_Andreas_Khevenh%C3%BCller,_Count_of_Aschelberg-Frankenburg" class="mw-redirect" title="Ludwig Andreas Khevenhüller, Count of Aschelberg-Frankenburg">Khevenhüller</a> at Vienna, and the Austrians planned an offensive winter campaign against the Franco-Bavarian forces in Bohemia and the small Bavarian army that remained on the Danube to defend the electorate.</p>
<p>Meanwhile the Saxon-born Maurice de Saxe and a small French force had stormed Prague on 26 November 1741, <a href="/wiki/Francis_I,_Holy_Roman_Emperor" title="Francis I, Holy Roman Emperor">Francis Stephen</a>, husband of Maria Theresa, who commanded the Austrians in Bohemia, moving too slowly to save the fortress. The Elector of Bavaria, who now styled himself <a href="/wiki/Archduke_of_Austria" class="mw-redirect" title="Archduke of Austria">Archduke of Austria</a>, was crowned King of Bohemia (9 December 1741) and elected to the imperial throne as <a href="/wiki/Charles_VII,_Holy_Roman_Emperor" title="Charles VII, Holy Roman Emperor">Charles VII</a> (24 January 1742), but no active measures were undertaken.</p>
<p>In Bohemia the month of December was occupied in mere skirmishes. On the Danube, Khevenhüller, the best general in the Austrian service, advanced on 27 December, swiftly drove back the allies, shut them up in <a href="/wiki/Linz" title="Linz">Linz</a>, and pressed on into Bavaria.<sup id="cite_ref-33" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-33">[33]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Munich" title="Munich">Munich</a> itself surrendered to the Austrians on the <a href="/wiki/Coronation" title="Coronation">coronation</a> day of Charles VII.</p>
<p>At the close of this first act of the campaign the French, under the old Marshal <a href="/wiki/Fran%C3%A7ois-Marie,_1st_duc_de_Broglie" title="François-Marie, 1st duc de Broglie">de Broglie</a>, maintained a precarious foothold in central Bohemia, menaced by the main army of the Austrians, and Khevenhüller was ranging unopposed in Bavaria. Frederick made a secret truce with Austria and thus, lay inactive in Silesia.</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Campaigns_of_1742">Campaigns of 1742</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=War_of_the_Austrian_Succession&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5" title="Edit section: Campaigns of 1742">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:20131020142107!Martin_van_Meytens_007.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/19/20131020142107%21Martin_van_Meytens_007.jpg/220px-20131020142107%21Martin_van_Meytens_007.jpg" width="220" height="272" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/19/20131020142107%21Martin_van_Meytens_007.jpg/330px-20131020142107%21Martin_van_Meytens_007.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/1/19/20131020142107%21Martin_van_Meytens_007.jpg 2x" data-file-width="388" data-file-height="479" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:20131020142107!Martin_van_Meytens_007.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
<a href="/wiki/Prince_Charles_Alexander_of_Lorraine" title="Prince Charles Alexander of Lorraine">Prince Charles Alexander of Lorraine</a></div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Frederick had hoped by the truce to secure Silesia, for which alone he was fighting; although allied with the French, he had no wish to see them become the dominant power in Germany through the destruction of Austria. For their part, the French had aspirations to divide most of the Habsburg territories between themselves, Prussia, Bavaria and Saxony. But with the successes of Khevenhüller and the enthusiastic "insurrection" of Hungary, Maria Theresa's opposition became firmer, and she divulged the provisions of the <a href="/wiki/Armistice" title="Armistice">truce</a>, to compromise Frederick with his allies. The war recommenced. Frederick had not rested idle on his laurels. In the uneventful summer campaign of 1741 he had found time to begin the reorganisation of his cavalry. The training of the Prussian cavalry had been neglected by Frederick's father—King Frederick William I.<sup id="cite_ref-Asprey-p208_34-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Asprey-p208-34">[34]</a></sup> Probably because he himself was an infantryman to his core, the training of the cavalry had also been overlooked by the "<a href="/wiki/Leopold_I,_Prince_of_Anhalt-Dessau" title="Leopold I, Prince of Anhalt-Dessau">Old Dessauer</a>" who was the true genius behind the Prussian Army.<sup id="cite_ref-Asprey-p208_34-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Asprey-p208-34">[34]</a></sup> Frederick had been disappointed by the performance of his cavalry at the Battle of Mollwitz.<sup id="cite_ref-35" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-35">[35]</a></sup> However, as a result of Frederick's training of the cavalry, over the summer of 1741, the Prussian cavalry would soon acquit themselves much better in the coming battles of the First Silesian War. Before long the cavalry would be more efficient than the Prussian infantry.</p>
<p>The Bavarian Emperor Charles VII, whose territories were overrun by the Austrians, asked him to create a diversion by invading Moravia. In December 1741, therefore, the Prussian general field marshal <a href="/wiki/Kurt_Christoph_Graf_von_Schwerin" title="Kurt Christoph Graf von Schwerin">Kurt Christoph Graf von Schwerin</a> crossed the border and captured <a href="/wiki/Olmutz" class="mw-redirect" title="Olmutz">Olmutz</a>. <a href="/wiki/K%C5%82odzko" title="Kłodzko">Glatz</a> also was <a href="/wiki/Siege" title="Siege">invested</a>, and the Prussian army was concentrated about Olomouc in January 1742. A combined <a href="/wiki/Military_strategy" title="Military strategy">plan of operations</a> was made by the French, Saxons and Prussians for the rescue of Linz. But Linz soon fell. Broglie on the <a href="/wiki/Vltava" title="Vltava">Vltava</a>, weakened by the departure of the Bavarians to oppose Khevenhüller, and of the Saxons to join forces with Frederick, was in no condition to take the offensive, and large forces under <a href="/wiki/Prince_Charles_Alexander_of_Lorraine" title="Prince Charles Alexander of Lorraine">Prince Charles of Lorraine</a> lay in his front from <a href="/wiki/Budweis" class="mw-redirect" title="Budweis">Budweis</a> to <a href="/wiki/Jihlava" title="Jihlava">Jihlava</a> (Iglau). Frederick's march was made towards Iglau in the first place. <a href="/wiki/Brno" title="Brno">Brno</a> was invested about the same time (February), but the direction of the march was changed, and instead of moving against Prince Charles, Frederick pushed on southwards by <a href="/wiki/Znojmo" title="Znojmo">Znojmo</a> and <a href="/wiki/Mikulov" title="Mikulov">Mikulov</a>. The extreme outposts of the Prussians appeared before Vienna. But Frederick's advance was a mere foray, and Prince Charles, leaving a screen of troops in front of Broglie, marched to cut off the Prussians from Silesia, while the Hungarian <a href="/wiki/Conscription" title="Conscription">levies</a> poured into <a href="/wiki/Upper_Silesia" title="Upper Silesia">Upper Silesia</a> by the <a href="/wiki/Jablunkov_Pass" title="Jablunkov Pass">Jablunkov Pass</a>. The Saxons, discontented and demoralised, soon marched off to their own country, and Frederick with his Prussians fell back by <a href="/wiki/Svitavy" title="Svitavy">Svitavy</a> and <a href="/wiki/Litomy%C5%A1l" title="Litomyšl">Litomyšl</a> to <a href="/wiki/Kutn%C3%A1_Hora" title="Kutná Hora">Kutná Hora</a> in Bohemia, where he was in touch with Broglie on the one hand and (Glatz having now surrendered) with Silesia on the other. No defence of Olomouc was attempted, and the small Prussian corps remaining in Moravia fell back towards Upper Silesia.</p>
<p>Prince Charles marched past Jihlava and Teutsch (Deutsch) Brod on Kutná Hora in pursuit of Frederick. On 17 May 1742 Frederick turned around and faced the Austrian forces that were pursuing him.<sup id="cite_ref-36" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-36">[36]</a></sup> He fought the Austrians in what has become known as the <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Chotusitz" title="Battle of Chotusitz">Battle of Chotusitz</a>. After a severe struggle Frederick won a major Prussian victory. At Chotusitz, it was Frederick's newly reorganised and trained cavalry that really won the victory<sup id="cite_ref-37" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-37">[37]</a></sup> and compensated for their previous failings. The cavalry's conduct gave an earnest prospect of its future glory, not only by its <a href="/wiki/Charge_(warfare)" title="Charge (warfare)">charges</a> on the battlefield, but by its vigorous pursuit of the defeated Austrians.</p>
<p>Almost at the same time the Battle of Chotusitz was occurring, French Field Marshal <a href="/wiki/Fran%C3%A7ois_Marie_de_Broglie" class="mw-redirect" title="François Marie de Broglie">François Broglie</a> fell upon a part of the Austrians left on the Vltava and won a small, but morally and politically important, success in the action of <a href="/wiki/Zah%C3%A1j%C3%AD_(%C4%8Cesk%C3%A9_Bud%C4%9Bjovice_District)" title="Zahájí (České Budějovice District)">Sahay</a>, near Budweis (24 May 1742). Frederick did not propose another combined movement. Frederick's victory at Chotusitz, along with the victory of Field Marshal Broglie, persuaded Maria Theresa to seek peace even if it meant ceding away Silesia to make good her position elsewhere.<sup id="cite_ref-Jay_Luvaas_p._4_25-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Jay_Luvaas_p._4-25">[25]</a></sup> Accordingly, a separate peace between Prussia and Austria was signed at <a href="/wiki/Wroc%C5%82aw" title="Wrocław">Breslau</a> on 11 June 1742, which drew the <b>First Silesian War</b> to a close.<sup id="cite_ref-38" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-38">[38]</a></sup> However, the larger War of the Austrian Succession continued.</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Campaign_of_1743">Campaign of 1743</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=War_of_the_Austrian_Succession&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6" title="Edit section: Campaign of 1743">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>The year 1743 opened disastrously for the forces of the new Holy Roman Emperor—Charles VII. The French and Bavarian armies were not working well together, and Field Marshal Broglie had been placed in command of the allied army in Bavaria.<sup id="cite_ref-39" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-39">[39]</a></sup> This created tension between Broglie and the Bavarian commanders. Broglie openly quarrelled with the Bavarian field marshal <a href="/wiki/Friedrich_Heinrich_von_Seckendorff" title="Friedrich Heinrich von Seckendorff">Friedrich Heinrich von Seckendorff</a>. No connected resistance was offered to the converging march of Prince Charles's army along the Danube, Khevenhüller from Salzburg towards southern Bavaria, and Prince Lobkowitz from Bohemia towards the <a href="/wiki/Naab" title="Naab">Naab</a>. The Bavarians, under the command of Count Minuzzi, suffered a severe reverse at the town of <a href="/wiki/Simbach,_Dingolfing-Landau" title="Simbach, Dingolfing-Landau">Simbach</a> near <a href="/wiki/Braunau_am_Inn" title="Braunau am Inn">Braunau</a> on 9 May 1743 at the hands of Prince Charles of Lorraine.<sup id="cite_ref-40" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-40">[40]</a></sup></p>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:George_II_of_Great_Britain-01.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1e/George_II_of_Great_Britain-01.jpg/220px-George_II_of_Great_Britain-01.jpg" width="220" height="270" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1e/George_II_of_Great_Britain-01.jpg/330px-George_II_of_Great_Britain-01.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1e/George_II_of_Great_Britain-01.jpg/440px-George_II_of_Great_Britain-01.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1220" data-file-height="1500" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:George_II_of_Great_Britain-01.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
<a href="/wiki/George_II_of_Great_Britain" title="George II of Great Britain">George II of Great Britain</a></div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Now an Anglo–Allied army commanded by King <a href="/wiki/George_II_of_Great_Britain" title="George II of Great Britain">George II</a> retreated down the <a href="/wiki/Main_River" class="mw-redirect" title="Main River">Main River</a> to the village of <a href="/wiki/Hanau" title="Hanau">Hanau</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-41" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-41">[41]</a></sup> This army had been formed on the lower Rhine upon the withdrawal of the French (Westphalian) Army under the command of <a href="/wiki/Count_Maillebois" class="mw-redirect" title="Count Maillebois">Count Maillebois</a>. This British army became known as the "Pragmatic Army," because it was a confederation of states that supported the <a href="/wiki/Pragmatic_Sanction_of_1713" title="Pragmatic Sanction of 1713">Pragmatic Sanction of 1713</a> agreements to recognize <a href="/wiki/Maria_Theresa" title="Maria Theresa">Maria Theresa</a> as sovereign of the Habsburg Empire. The Pragmatic Army had been advancing southward up the <a href="/wiki/Main_(river)" title="Main (river)">Main</a> into <a href="/wiki/Neckar" title="Neckar">Neckar</a> country prior to this retreat in the summer of 1743. A French army, under Marshal <a href="/wiki/Adrien_Maurice,_duc_de_Noailles" class="mw-redirect" title="Adrien Maurice, duc de Noailles">Noailles</a>, was being collected on the middle Rhine to deal with this new force. Marshal Noailles correctly anticipated that given the problems faced by the Pragmatic Army, George II would take the entire British Pragmatic Army back down the Main.<sup id="cite_ref-42" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-42">[42]</a></sup> Marshal Noailles made plans to lay a trap for the Pragmatic Army and destroy it. However, Marshal Noailles's ally Marshal Broglie was now in full retreat. Strong places of Bavaria were surrendered one after the other to Prince Charles. Marshal Noailles's French and Bavarian army was suddenly outnumbered by the Pragmatic Army 35,000 soldiers to 26,000 soldiers.<sup id="cite_ref-43" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-43">[43]</a></sup> Before Marshal Noailles could order a retreat, his army was surprised and defeated on 27 June 1743 by King George at <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Dettingen" title="Battle of Dettingen">Dettingen</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-44" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-44">[44]</a></sup></p>
<p>King Frederick of Prussia was terrified by the defeat at Dettingen.<sup id="cite_ref-Robert_B._Asprey_p._275_45-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Robert_B._Asprey_p._275-45">[45]</a></sup> Frederick saw that he now faced a coalition of enemies that included Austria, Britain and Russia.<sup id="cite_ref-Robert_B._Asprey_p._275_45-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Robert_B._Asprey_p._275-45">[45]</a></sup> However, Frederick soon realised that the coalition against him was not as strong as it first appeared. Neither Austria nor the British knew how to exploit their victory at Dettingen.<sup id="cite_ref-Robert_B._Asprey_p._275_45-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Robert_B._Asprey_p._275-45">[45]</a></sup> Marshal Noailles was driven almost to the Rhine by King George. The French and Bavarian army had been completely outmanoeuvred and was in a position of the greatest danger between <a href="/wiki/Aschaffenburg" title="Aschaffenburg">Aschaffenburg</a> and <a href="/wiki/Hanau" title="Hanau">Hanau</a> in the <a href="/wiki/Defile_(geography)" title="Defile (geography)">defile</a> formed by the <a href="/wiki/Spessart" title="Spessart">Spessart</a> Hills and the river Main. Yet the British Pragmatic Army did not quickly follow up the attack. Thus, Marshal Noailles had time to block the outlet and had posts all around. At this point, the allied troops had to force their way through the French and Bavarian lines. Still, because of the heavy losses inflicted on the French, the <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Dettingen" title="Battle of Dettingen">Battle of Dettingen</a> and the follow up is justly reckoned as a notable victory of Anglo-Austrian-Hanoverian arms.</p>
<p>The coalition against Frederick was suddenly weakened when the St. Petersburg court discovered a plot to overthrow <a href="/wiki/Elizabeth_of_Russia" title="Elizabeth of Russia">Tsarina Elisabeth</a> and bring back the child <a href="/wiki/Ivan_VI" class="mw-redirect" title="Ivan VI">Ivan VI</a> as Tsar, with his mother <a href="/wiki/Grand_Duchess_Anna_Leopoldovna_of_Russia" class="mw-redirect" title="Grand Duchess Anna Leopoldovna of Russia">Grand Duchess Anna Leopoldovna</a> serving as regent for the child.<sup id="cite_ref-Robert_B._Asprey_p._275_45-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Robert_B._Asprey_p._275-45">[45]</a></sup> Matters were made much worse for the allies against Frederick when an Austrian envoy <a href="/wiki/Antoniotto_Botta_Adorno" title="Antoniotto Botta Adorno">Antoniotto Botta Adorno</a> was found to be intimately involved in the plot. Indeed, the plot became known as the "Botta Conspiracy."<sup id="cite_ref-46" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-46">[46]</a></sup> The Botta-attempted coup redounded badly not only against Austria, but also against the Saxon and British courts.<sup id="cite_ref-Robert_B._Asprey_p._275_45-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Robert_B._Asprey_p._275-45">[45]</a></sup> Frederick's initial indifference to a treaty with Russia now changed to enthusiasm in the light of the fallout from the Botta Conspiracy.<sup id="cite_ref-47" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-47">[47]</a></sup></p>
<p>Marshal Broglie, worn out by age and exertions, was soon replaced by Marshal <a href="/wiki/Fran%C3%A7ois_de_Franquetot,_Duc_de_Coigny" class="mw-redirect" title="François de Franquetot, Duc de Coigny">Coigny</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-48" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-48">[48]</a></sup> Both Broglie and Noailles were now on the strict defensive behind the Rhine. Not a single French soldier remained in Germany, and Prince Charles prepared to force the passage of the Rhine river in the <a href="/wiki/Breisgau" title="Breisgau">Breisgau</a> while George II, King of Britain, moved forward via <a href="/wiki/Mainz" title="Mainz">Mainz</a> to co-operate by drawing upon himself the attention of both the French marshals. The Anglo-allied army took <a href="/wiki/Worms,_Germany" title="Worms, Germany">Worms</a>, but after several unsuccessful attempts to cross the Rhine river, Prince Charles went into winter quarters. The king followed his example, drawing his troops to the north, to deal, if necessary, with the army which the French were collecting on the frontier of the <a href="/wiki/Southern_Netherlands" title="Southern Netherlands">Southern Netherlands</a>. Austria, Britain, the Dutch Republic and Sardinia were now allied. Saxony changed sides and the entry of Sweden had offset the loss of Russia to the allies. Thus, Sweden and Russia neutralised each other (<a href="/wiki/Peace_of_%C3%85bo" class="mw-redirect" title="Peace of Åbo">Peace of Åbo</a>, August 1743). Frederick was still quiescent. France, Spain and Bavaria actively continued the struggle against Maria Theresa.</p>
<p>While the Battle of Dettingen and Russian Botta plot were capturing all the attention during the summer of 1743, negotiations between the British, the Austrians and Sardinians were proceeding quietly in the city of <a href="/wiki/Worms,_Germany" title="Worms, Germany">Worms</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-49" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-49">[49]</a></sup> The Austrians were desperately afraid that Frederick II would soon be invading the Austrian domains again. Thus, the Austrians sought a separate peace with Sardinia in Italy. Under the terms of the <a href="/wiki/Treaty_of_Worms_(1743)" title="Treaty of Worms (1743)">Treaty of Worms</a>, which was signed on 13 September 1743, the Austrian Habsburgs surrendered all territory in Italy located west of the <a href="/wiki/Ticino_River" class="mw-redirect" title="Ticino River">Ticino River</a> and <a href="/wiki/Lake_Maggiore" title="Lake Maggiore">Lake Maggiore</a> to Sardinia.<sup id="cite_ref-50" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-50">[50]</a></sup> Additionally some lands south of the Po River were also given to Sardinia.<sup id="cite_ref-51" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-51">[51]</a></sup> In exchange, Sardinia renounced its claim to Milan, guaranteed the Pragmatic Sanction and agreed to provide 40,000 troops for a joint Italian army to fight the Bourbons.</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Campaign_of_1744">Campaign of 1744</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=War_of_the_Austrian_Succession&amp;action=edit&amp;section=7" title="Edit section: Campaign of 1744">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Louis_XV_by_Maurice-Quentin_de_La_Tour.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/51/Louis_XV_by_Maurice-Quentin_de_La_Tour.jpg/220px-Louis_XV_by_Maurice-Quentin_de_La_Tour.jpg" width="220" height="266" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/51/Louis_XV_by_Maurice-Quentin_de_La_Tour.jpg/330px-Louis_XV_by_Maurice-Quentin_de_La_Tour.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/51/Louis_XV_by_Maurice-Quentin_de_La_Tour.jpg/440px-Louis_XV_by_Maurice-Quentin_de_La_Tour.jpg 2x" data-file-width="636" data-file-height="768" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Louis_XV_by_Maurice-Quentin_de_La_Tour.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
<a href="/wiki/Louis_XV_of_France" title="Louis XV of France">Louis XV of France</a> by <a href="/wiki/Maurice_Quentin_de_La_Tour" title="Maurice Quentin de La Tour">Maurice Quentin de La Tour</a> (1748) Pastel painting</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>With 1744 began the <a href="/wiki/Second_Silesian_War" class="mw-redirect" title="Second Silesian War">Second Silesian War</a>. Frederick of Prussia was disquieted by the universal success of the Austrians and their alliance with Sardinia. Accordingly, he secretly concluded another fresh alliance with <a href="/wiki/Louis_XV_of_France" title="Louis XV of France">Louis XV of France</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-52" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-52">[52]</a></sup> France had posed hitherto as an auxiliary, its officers in Germany had worn the Bavarian <a href="/wiki/Cockade" title="Cockade">cockade</a>, and only with Britain was it officially at war. France now declared war directly upon Austria and Sardinia (April 1744).</p>
<p>At this point, France also planned a diversion which they hope would cause Britain to leave the war. A French army was assembled at <a href="/wiki/Dunkirk,_France" class="mw-redirect" title="Dunkirk, France">Dunkirk</a> to support the cause of <a href="/wiki/Charles_Edward_Stuart" title="Charles Edward Stuart">Charles Edward Stuart</a> (Bonnie Prince Charlie) in <a href="/wiki/Planned_French_Invasion_of_Britain_(1744)" class="mw-redirect" title="Planned French Invasion of Britain (1744)">an invasion of Great Britain</a>. Prince Charles was son of <a href="/wiki/James_Francis_Edward_Stuart" title="James Francis Edward Stuart">James Francis Edward Stuart</a>, Stuart pretender to the British throne, who was the son of <a href="/wiki/James_II_of_England" title="James II of England">James II</a> the last Catholic and last Stuart king of England. James II had been deposed as the King of England in 1688 in favour of his daughter, Mary, and her husband the Protestant Prince of Orange--<a href="/wiki/William_III_of_England" title="William III of England">William III</a> of the house of Orange-Nassau. There remained a significant element of the population of the British Isles that hoped for the return of the Stuart family as monarchs. King <a href="/wiki/Louis_XIV_of_France" title="Louis XIV of France">Louis XIV of France</a> had shown great support for Stuart cause. Indeed, in 1715, France had sponsored an uprising in Scotland, which the pretender James had joined, but it was defeated. Forbidden to return to France by the new king, Louis XV, James sought sanctuary elsewhere. Finally, <a href="/wiki/Pope_Clement_XI" title="Pope Clement XI">Pope Clement XI</a> offered James and his family the use of <a href="/wiki/Palazzo_Muti" title="Palazzo Muti">Palazzo Muti</a> and a lifetime annuity of 8,000 Roman <a href="/wiki/Scudi" class="mw-redirect" title="Scudi">scudi</a>. It was here, in the Palazzo Muti, that Charles Edward Stuart, was born and had lived his whole life.</p>
<p>Charles had much more charisma than his father, and now Louis XV was favourably disposed toward helping him create another uprising in Scotland. Louis XV sent Drummond of Balhaldy as an emissary to the Stuart "court" in Rome.<sup id="cite_ref-53" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-53">[53]</a></sup> French plans called for Charles to be in Dunkirk, France, to assemble with the fleet on 10 January 1744, yet Balhaldy had only arrived in Rome on 19 December 1743.<sup id="cite_ref-54" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-54">[54]</a></sup> Thus there was very little time to waste. On 23 December 1743, Charles' father named him "<a href="/wiki/Prince_regent" title="Prince regent">Prince Regent</a>" so that Charles could act in his own name. In the spring of 1744, Prince Charles secretly arrived in France and was about to board the ships that would take him to England. However, on the night before he was to board, a fierce storm blew up (this storm became known as the "Protestant Wind") and wrecked or dispersed the entire fleet.<sup id="cite_ref-55" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-55">[55]</a></sup> The violent storms had wrecked the crossing attempt, and the planned invasion was abandoned. However, Charles did not give up hope of restoring the Stuart family to the throne of England.</p>
<p>During naval operations that were possible preparations for the return of Charles Edward Stuart to England and a coordinated French invasion of England, there occurred, on 22 February 1744, the largest sea battle of the war.<sup id="cite_ref-Browning-p155_56-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Browning-p155-56">[56]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Toulon_(1744)" title="Battle of Toulon (1744)">This naval battle</a> took place in the Mediterranean off the coast of <a href="/wiki/Toulon" title="Toulon">Toulon</a>, France. A large British fleet under the command of Admiral <a href="/wiki/Thomas_Mathews" title="Thomas Mathews">Thomas Mathews</a> with Rear Admiral <a href="/wiki/Richard_Lestock" title="Richard Lestock">Richard Lestock</a>, second in command was blockading the French coast. A smaller French and Spanish naval force attacked the British blockade and damaged some of the British ships forcing the British to withdraw and seek repairs. Thus, the British blockade of the French coast was relieved and the Spanish fleet apparently controlled the Mediterranean Sea. A Spanish squadron took refuge in the harbour at <a href="/wiki/Toulon" title="Toulon">Toulon</a>. The British fleet watched this squadron carefully from a harbour a short distance to the east. On 21 February 1744, the Spanish ships put to sea with a French fleet. Admiral Mathews took his British fleet and attacked the Spanish fleet from 22 February until 23 February 1744 in what has become known as the Battle of Toulon. However, because of mis-communication and possibly treachery on the part of Rear Admiral Lestock, the smaller Spanish fleet was allowed to escape. With the knowledge that a larger French fleet was sailing to the rescue the British ships broke off combat and retreated to the northeast.</p>
<p>Although technically the Battle of Toulon was regarded as a victory for Britain,<sup id="cite_ref-57" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-57">[57]</a></sup> in Britain it was feared by the public that the combined French and Spanish ships were making for the <a href="/wiki/Straits_of_Gibraltar" class="mw-redirect" title="Straits of Gibraltar">Straits of Gibraltar</a> and for a gathering of ships at <a href="/wiki/Brest,_France" title="Brest, France">Brest</a> for a <a href="/wiki/Planned_French_Invasion_of_Britain_(1744)" class="mw-redirect" title="Planned French Invasion of Britain (1744)">planned invasion of England</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Smith-p243_58-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Smith-p243-58">[58]</a></sup> As a consequence, bitter recriminations were brought against Admiral Mathews for letting this Spanish-French fleet get away and, subsequently, placing England in danger of invasion. Consequently, both Mathews and Lestock were tried in naval court. Lestock was acquitted (unjustly according to some) while Mathews was found guilty (also regarded as an injustice by some commentators).<sup id="cite_ref-Browning-p155_56-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Browning-p155-56">[56]</a></sup></p>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:252px;"><a href="/wiki/File:OHM_-_Bayrischer_Krieg_1.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5a/OHM_-_Bayrischer_Krieg_1.jpg/250px-OHM_-_Bayrischer_Krieg_1.jpg" width="250" height="167" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5a/OHM_-_Bayrischer_Krieg_1.jpg/375px-OHM_-_Bayrischer_Krieg_1.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5a/OHM_-_Bayrischer_Krieg_1.jpg/500px-OHM_-_Bayrischer_Krieg_1.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2560" data-file-height="1712" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:OHM_-_Bayrischer_Krieg_1.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Warfare between Deggendorf and Vilshofen, Bavaria</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Meanwhile, on the battlefields in northern Europe, Louis XV in person, with 90,000 men, invaded the <a href="/wiki/Austrian_Netherlands" title="Austrian Netherlands">Austrian Netherlands</a><sup id="cite_ref-59" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-59">[59]</a></sup> and took <a href="/wiki/Menen" title="Menen">Menin</a> and <a href="/wiki/Ypres" title="Ypres">Ypres</a> in July 1744.<sup id="cite_ref-60" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-60">[60]</a></sup> His presumed opponent, although shorn of the Russians, still consisted the same allied army, previously commanded by King George II, and composed of British, Dutch, German (Hanoverian) and Austrian troops.</p>
<p>The French put four armies into the field.<sup id="cite_ref-Browning-p172_61-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Browning-p172-61">[61]</a></sup> On the Rhine, Marshal Coigny had 57,000 troops up against 70,000 allied troops under the command of Prince Charles.<sup id="cite_ref-62" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-62">[62]</a></sup> A fresh army of over 30,000 soldiers under the <a href="/wiki/Louis_Fran%C3%A7ois_I_de_Bourbon,_prince_de_Conti" class="mw-redirect" title="Louis François I de Bourbon, prince de Conti">Prince de Conti</a> was located between the <a href="/wiki/Meuse_River" class="mw-redirect" title="Meuse River">Meuse</a> and <a href="/wiki/Moselle_River" class="mw-redirect" title="Moselle River">Moselle</a> Rivers, which would later assist the Spaniards in Piedmont and Lombardy.<sup id="cite_ref-Browning-p172_61-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Browning-p172-61">[61]</a></sup> This plan was, however, at once dislocated by the advance of Prince Charles, who, assisted by the veteran Marshal <a href="/wiki/Otto_Ferdinand_von_Abensberg_und_Traun" title="Otto Ferdinand von Abensberg und Traun">Traun</a>, skillfully manoeuvred his allied army over the Rhine near <a href="/wiki/Philippsburg" title="Philippsburg">Philippsburg</a> on 1 July 1744 and captured the <a href="/wiki/Lines_of_Weissenburg" title="Lines of Weissenburg">lines of Weissenburg</a>, and cut off Marshal Coigny and his army from <a href="/wiki/Alsace" title="Alsace">Alsace</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-63" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-63">[63]</a></sup></p>
<p>A third French Army composed of 17,000 men under the command of <a href="/wiki/Fran%C3%A7ois-Henri_d%27Harcourt" title="François-Henri d'Harcourt">Duke d' Harcourt</a> kept Luxembourg at bay<sup id="cite_ref-Browning-p172_61-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Browning-p172-61">[61]</a></sup> Meanwhile, the fourth French army was the largest army that put to field in the summer of 1744. This was the Army of Flanders. Numbering 87,000 men and was officially under the command of the king of France—Louis XV, but in actuality Louis XV was being militarily advised by Marshal Noailles.<sup id="cite_ref-64" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-64">[64]</a></sup> As these French forces invaded the <a href="/wiki/Austrian_Netherlands" title="Austrian Netherlands">Austrian Netherlands</a>, they outnumbered the allied armies by about a four to three ratio.<sup id="cite_ref-Browning-p174_65-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Browning-p174-65">[65]</a></sup> Furthermore, as they marched into the Austrian Netherlands, they met a confused resistance offered by Dutch forces.<sup id="cite_ref-66" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-66">[66]</a></sup> Consequently, the French Army of Flanders made rapid progress across the Austrian Netherlands.<sup id="cite_ref-Browning-p174_65-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Browning-p174-65">[65]</a></sup> The situation became so desperate for the Dutch, that the Dutch government sent an envoy to the king of France to seek peace. This plea for peace was rejected by the French.<sup id="cite_ref-Browning-p174_65-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Browning-p174-65">[65]</a></sup></p>
<p>However, the situation in the Austrian Netherlands was changed abruptly by the successful crossing of the Rhine on 30 June 1744 by Prince Charles and his 70,000-man allied army.<sup id="cite_ref-Browning-p174_65-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Browning-p174-65">[65]</a></sup> Marshal Coigny, caught far in advance of the other French forces, cut his way back through the enemy at <a href="/wiki/Wissembourg" title="Wissembourg">Weissenburg</a> and withdrew towards <a href="/wiki/Strasbourg" title="Strasbourg">Strasbourg</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Browning-p175_67-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Browning-p175-67">[67]</a></sup> Louis XV now abandoned the invasion of the <a href="/wiki/Southern_Netherlands" title="Southern Netherlands">Southern Netherlands</a>, and his army moved down to take a decisive part in the war in Alsace and <a href="/wiki/Lorraine_(province)" class="mw-redirect" title="Lorraine (province)">Lorraine</a>.</p>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:252px;"><a href="/wiki/File:OHM_-_Bayrischer_Krieg_2.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/bc/OHM_-_Bayrischer_Krieg_2.jpg/250px-OHM_-_Bayrischer_Krieg_2.jpg" width="250" height="167" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/bc/OHM_-_Bayrischer_Krieg_2.jpg/375px-OHM_-_Bayrischer_Krieg_2.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/bc/OHM_-_Bayrischer_Krieg_2.jpg/500px-OHM_-_Bayrischer_Krieg_2.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2560" data-file-height="1712" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:OHM_-_Bayrischer_Krieg_2.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Military camp: war of the Austrian succession</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Finally on 12 July 1744, Frederick II of Prussia received confirmation that Prince Charles had taken his army beyond the Rhine and into France.<sup id="cite_ref-Browning-p175_67-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Browning-p175-67">[67]</a></sup> Thus, Frederick knew that Prince Charles would not be able to present any immediate problem to him in the east. Consequently, on 15 August 1744, Frederick II, crossed the Austrian frontier into Bohemia. By late August all 80,000 of his troops were in Bohemia.<sup id="cite_ref-68" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-68">[68]</a></sup> The attention and resources of Austria had been fully occupied for some time on a renewal of the war in Silesia. However, neither Maria Theresa nor her advisers had expected the Prussians to march as quickly as they did.<sup id="cite_ref-Asprey-p290_32-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Asprey-p290-32">[32]</a></sup> Accordingly, Frederick's invasion of Bohemia came as a surprise to the Austrian court and Frederick was almost unopposed in Bohemia. One column consisting of 40,000 troops, under Frederick's own command, passed through Saxony; another column of 16,000 men under the command of "<a href="/wiki/Leopold_II,_Prince_of_Anhalt-Dessau" title="Leopold II, Prince of Anhalt-Dessau">Young Dessauer</a>" passed through <a href="/wiki/Lusatia" title="Lusatia">Lusatia</a>, while a third consisting of 16,000 soldiers under Count Schwerin advanced from Silesia.<sup id="cite_ref-Browning-p181_69-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Browning-p181-69">[69]</a></sup> The destination for all three columns was Prague. The objective, was reached on 2 September. The city was surrounded and besieged. Six days later the Austrian garrison was compelled to surrender.<sup id="cite_ref-Jay_Luvaas_p._4_25-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Jay_Luvaas_p._4-25">[25]</a></sup> Scarcely had Prague surrendered to Frederick II than he was off marching southwards, leaving 5,000 soldiers under General Baron <a href="/w/index.php?title=Gottfried_Emanual_von_Einsiedel&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Gottfried Emanual von Einsiedel (page does not exist)">Gottfried Emanual von Einsiedel</a> to garrison Prague.<sup id="cite_ref-70" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-70">[70]</a></sup> Three days after the fall of Prague, Frederick marched with his army marching southwards and seized <a href="/wiki/T%C3%A1bor" title="Tábor">Tabor</a>, <a href="/wiki/Budweis" class="mw-redirect" title="Budweis">Budweis</a> and <a href="/wiki/Hlubok%C3%A1_nad_Vltavou" title="Hluboká nad Vltavou">Frauenberg</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-71" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-71">[71]</a></sup></p>
<p>Maria Theresa once again rose to the emergency, a new "insurrection" took the field in Hungary, and a corps of regulars was assembled to cover Vienna. Meanwhile, Austrian diplomats won over Saxony to the Austrian side.<sup id="cite_ref-72" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-72">[72]</a></sup> Because of Frederick's successful campaign in Bohemia, Prince Charles sought to withdraw from Alsace and cross the Rhine once again and strike at the Prussians. At this point the French had an excellent chance to strike at Prince Charles while he was in a vulnerable position—crossing the Rhine. However, the French military command was distracted and could not take any action at all and Prince Charles was able to cross the Rhine once again unmolested by the French. The French had been unable to act because they were thrown into confusion by King Louis XV suddenly becoming very ill with smallpox at <a href="/wiki/Metz" title="Metz">Metz</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Browning-p181_69-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Browning-p181-69">[69]</a></sup> The King's condition was so severe that many feared for his life. Only <a href="/wiki/Friedrich_Heinrich_von_Seckendorff" title="Friedrich Heinrich von Seckendorff">Count Seckendorf</a> commander of the Bavarians pursued Prince Charles. No move was made by the French, and Frederick, thus, found himself isolated and exposed to the combined attack of the Austrians and Saxons. Count Traun, summoned from the Rhine, held the king in check in Bohemia with a united force of Austrians and Saxons. The Hungarian irregulars also inflicted numerous minor reverses on the Prussians. Finally Prince Charles arrived with the main army from the west. The campaign resembled that of 1742: the Prussian retreat was closely watched, and the rearguard pressed hard. Prague fell, and Frederick was completely outmanoeuvred by the united forces of Prince Charles and Count Traun.<sup id="cite_ref-73" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-73">[73]</a></sup> Frederick was forced to retreat to Silesia with heavy losses. However, the Austrians gained no foothold in Silesia itself. On the Rhine, Louis XV, now recovered, had besieged and taken <a href="/wiki/Freiburg" class="mw-redirect" title="Freiburg">Freiburg</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-Browning-p196_74-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Browning-p196-74">[74]</a></sup> after which the forces left in the north were reinforced and besieged the strong places of <a href="/wiki/Southern_Netherlands" title="Southern Netherlands">Southern Netherlands</a>. There was also a slight war of manoeuvre on the middle Rhine.</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Campaign_of_1745">Campaign of 1745</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=War_of_the_Austrian_Succession&amp;action=edit&amp;section=8" title="Edit section: Campaign of 1745">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:302px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Hohenfriedeberg_-_Attack_of_Prussian_Infantry_-_1745.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9a/Hohenfriedeberg_-_Attack_of_Prussian_Infantry_-_1745.jpg/300px-Hohenfriedeberg_-_Attack_of_Prussian_Infantry_-_1745.jpg" width="300" height="145" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9a/Hohenfriedeberg_-_Attack_of_Prussian_Infantry_-_1745.jpg/450px-Hohenfriedeberg_-_Attack_of_Prussian_Infantry_-_1745.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9a/Hohenfriedeberg_-_Attack_of_Prussian_Infantry_-_1745.jpg/600px-Hohenfriedeberg_-_Attack_of_Prussian_Infantry_-_1745.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1920" data-file-height="931" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Hohenfriedeberg_-_Attack_of_Prussian_Infantry_-_1745.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Attack of the Prussian Infantry at the <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Hohenfriedberg" title="Battle of Hohenfriedberg">Battle of Hohenfriedberg</a> by <a href="/wiki/Carl_R%C3%B6chling" title="Carl Röchling">Carl Röchling</a></div>
</div>
</div>
<p>The year 1745 saw three of the greatest battles of the war: <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Hohenfriedberg" title="Battle of Hohenfriedberg">Hohenfriedberg</a>, <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Kesselsdorf" title="Battle of Kesselsdorf">Kesselsdorf</a> and <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Fontenoy" title="Battle of Fontenoy">Fontenoy</a>. The first event of the year was the formation of the <a href="/wiki/Quadruple_Alliance_(1745)" class="mw-redirect" title="Quadruple Alliance (1745)">Quadruple Alliance</a> of Britain, Austria, the Dutch Republic and Saxony, concluded at <a href="/wiki/Warsaw" title="Warsaw">Warsaw</a> on 8 January 1745 by the <a href="/wiki/Treaty_of_Warsaw_(1745)" title="Treaty of Warsaw (1745)">Treaty of Warsaw</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-75" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-75">[75]</a></sup> Twelve days later on 20 January 1745, the death of the Holy Roman Emperor--<a href="/wiki/Charles_VII,_Holy_Roman_Emperor" title="Charles VII, Holy Roman Emperor">Charles VII</a>—submitted the imperial title to a new election.<sup id="cite_ref-Browning-p196_74-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Browning-p196-74">[74]</a></sup> Charles VII's son and heir, <a href="/wiki/Maximilian_III_Joseph,_Elector_of_Bavaria" title="Maximilian III Joseph, Elector of Bavaria">Maximilian III</a> in Bavaria was not even considered a candidate for the Imperial throne. The Bavarian army was again unfortunate. Caught in its scattered winter quarters (action of Amberg, 7 Jan.), it was driven from point to point by a maneuver by the Austrian army under the joint command of <a href="/wiki/K%C3%A1roly_J%C3%B3zsef_Batthy%C3%A1ny" title="Károly József Batthyány">Count Batthyány</a>, Baron Bernklau and <a href="/wiki/Maximilian_Ulysses_Browne" title="Maximilian Ulysses Browne">Count Browne</a>. All Bavarian garrisons fled to the east. The Bavarian Army under the command of <a href="/w/index.php?title=Count_T%C3%B6rring&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Count Törring (page does not exist)">Count Törring</a> was divided and paralyzed.<sup id="cite_ref-Browning-p203_76-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Browning-p203-76">[76]</a></sup> The French in the area under <a href="/wiki/Henri_Fran%C3%A7ois,_comte_de_S%C3%A9gur" title="Henri François, comte de Ségur">Count Ségur</a> marched to save the day. Count Sègur's force out-numbered the Austrian army under Count Batthyany, yet Sègur and the French army were defeated at the <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Pfaffenhofen" title="Battle of Pfaffenhofen">Battle of Pfaffenhofen</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Browning-p203_76-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Browning-p203-76">[76]</a></sup> The young elector <a href="/wiki/Maximilian_III_Joseph,_Elector_of_Bavaria" title="Maximilian III Joseph, Elector of Bavaria">Maximilian III Joseph</a> had to abandon Munich once more.
