The <a href="/wiki/Treaty_of_F%C3%BCssen" title="Treaty of Füssen">Peace of Füssen</a> followed on 22 April 1745, by which Maximilian III secured his hereditary states on condition of supporting the candidature of the Grand-Duke Francis, consort of Maria Theresa. The "imperial" army ceased <i>ipso facto</i> to exist.</p>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:302px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Battle_of_Fontenoy_03.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/33/Battle_of_Fontenoy_03.jpg/300px-Battle_of_Fontenoy_03.jpg" width="300" height="188" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/33/Battle_of_Fontenoy_03.jpg/450px-Battle_of_Fontenoy_03.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/33/Battle_of_Fontenoy_03.jpg/600px-Battle_of_Fontenoy_03.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1836" data-file-height="1151" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Battle_of_Fontenoy_03.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
<i>The Battle of Fontenoy</i> between the French and the British, by <a href="/wiki/Blarenberghe" title="Blarenberghe">Louis-Nicolas van Blarenberghe</a></div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Frederick II of Prussia was again isolated. No help was to be expected from France, whose efforts this year were centred on the Flanders campaign. Indeed, on 31 March 1745, before Frederick ever took the field in the spring of 1745, Louis XV and the Marshal of France <a href="/wiki/Maurice_de_Saxe" title="Maurice de Saxe">Maurice de Saxe</a>, commanding an army of 95,000 men, the largest force in the war, marched down the <a href="/wiki/Scheldt_River" class="mw-redirect" title="Scheldt River">Scheldt River</a> valley and had besieged <a href="/wiki/Tournai" title="Tournai">Tournay</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-77" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-77">[77]</a></sup> Tournay was defended by a Dutch garrison of 7,000 soldiers.<sup id="cite_ref-78" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-78">[78]</a></sup> In May 1745, a British army under the command of the <a href="/wiki/William_Augustus,_Duke_of_Cumberland" class="mw-redirect" title="William Augustus, Duke of Cumberland">Duke of Cumberland</a> attempted to break the French siege and relieve Tournay. Maurice (who had just recently been appointed a Marshal in the French army) had very good intelligence and knew the road that Cumberland was using to attack his forces besieging forces. Thus, Maurice could select the battlefield. Maurice chose to attack the British allied army on a plain on the east side of the Scheldt River about two miles southeast of Tournay near the town of <a href="/wiki/Antoing" title="Antoing">Fontenoy</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-79" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-79">[79]</a></sup> There the <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Fontenoy" title="Battle of Fontenoy">Battle of Fontenoy</a> was fought on 11 May 1745. Fighting began at 5:00 AM with a French artillery barrage of the British-Allied forces, who were still attempting to move into their proper positions for their anticipated attack on Tournay. By noon, Cumberland's troops had ground to a halt and discipline had begun to dissolve. The British-Allied army sought cover in a retreat.<sup id="cite_ref-80" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-80">[80]</a></sup> It was a victory for the French that captured the attention of Europe because it overturned the mystique of British military superiority and it pointed out the importance of artillery.<sup id="cite_ref-81" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-81">[81]</a></sup> On 20 June 1745, after the Battle on Fontenoy, the fortress of Tournay surrendered to the French.<sup id="cite_ref-82" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-82">[82]</a></sup></p>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:MarechalMauricedeSaxedeLaTour.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7e/MarechalMauricedeSaxedeLaTour.jpg/220px-MarechalMauricedeSaxedeLaTour.jpg" width="220" height="286" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7e/MarechalMauricedeSaxedeLaTour.jpg/330px-MarechalMauricedeSaxedeLaTour.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7e/MarechalMauricedeSaxedeLaTour.jpg/440px-MarechalMauricedeSaxedeLaTour.jpg 2x" data-file-width="538" data-file-height="700" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:MarechalMauricedeSaxedeLaTour.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Marshal General <a href="/wiki/Maurice_de_Saxe" title="Maurice de Saxe">Maurice de Saxe</a></div>
</div>
</div>
<p>In the summer of 1745, the French once more decided to take up <a href="/wiki/Charles_Edward_Stuart" title="Charles Edward Stuart">Charles Edward Stuart</a>'s claim to the British throne. The goal was to start a revolt in Scotland which would divert British attention away from the war on the mainland in Europe, and may even require Britain to leave the war altogether. On 23 July 1745, Charles landed on the island of <a href="/wiki/Eriskay" title="Eriskay">Eriskay</a> in the Hebrides, north-west of the mainland of Scotland.<sup id="cite_ref-83" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-83">[83]</a></sup> On 25 July 1745, Charles set sail again for the mainland. By the end of August 1745, they had landed Charles in Scotland and he had started issuing calls for troops loyal to the <a href="/wiki/Jacobitism" title="Jacobitism">Jacobite</a> cause of placing him on the throne.<sup id="cite_ref-Browning-p240_84-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Browning-p240-84">[84]</a></sup> Already, Charles had collected 1,300 Scots prepared to fight in his Jacobite army.<sup id="cite_ref-Browning-p240_84-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Browning-p240-84">[84]</a></sup> Defence of the Hanovarian rule of King George II in Great Britain fell to General Sir <a href="/wiki/John_Cope_(British_Army_officer)" title="John Cope (British Army officer)">John Cope</a>, a veteran of the Battle of Dettingen. On 31 August 1745, Cope marched north with about 2,000 British government soldiers.<sup id="cite_ref-Browning-p240_84-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Browning-p240-84">[84]</a></sup> Charles reached <a href="/wiki/Perth,_Scotland" title="Perth, Scotland">Perth</a> on 18 September 1745 and <a href="/wiki/Edinburgh" title="Edinburgh">Edinburgh</a> surrendered to him on 27 September 1745.<sup id="cite_ref-85" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-85">[85]</a></sup> When Cope brought his army up to the town of <a href="/wiki/Prestonpans" title="Prestonpans">Prestonpans</a>, Scotland on 1 October 1745, he chose a stubble field that he felt was well protected, on which to encamp his troops. However, it was not as safe as he thought and at sunrise the next morning, 2 October 1745, Charles's Scottish troops attacked and defeated the British government army.<sup id="cite_ref-86" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-86">[86]</a></sup> With the government army defeat at Prestonpans, it appeared that all Scotland belonged to Charles. By November 1745, his army consisted of 5,000 infantry men and 300 cavalry.<sup id="cite_ref-87" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-87">[87]</a></sup> In mid-November 1745 it crossed the border from Scotland and invaded England.</p>
<p>As the Jacobite army moved south into England, Charles kept assuring his troops that aid and reinforcements from English Jacobites would be arriving at any time. This aide and reinforcements were desperately needed as the Jacobites were badly outnumbered by the three British government armies already in the field.<sup id="cite_ref-88" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-88">[88]</a></sup> Finally on 6 December 1745, at Derby in the English midlands, Charles was reluctantly persuaded by his senior officers to turn back to Scotland.<sup id="cite_ref-89" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-89">[89]</a></sup> Upon hearing about the turnabout in Derby, the French gave up on their plans for an invasion of England.<sup id="cite_ref-90" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-90">[90]</a></sup> The Jacobites felt they could more securely fight the Hanovarians in a defensive battle on Scottish soil rather than fighting the British government army in England. On 17 January 1746, at the <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Falkirk_Muir" title="Battle of Falkirk Muir">Battle of Falkirk Muir</a>, 8,000 Scots, the largest amount of troops gathered by the Jacobite cause during the uprising defeated 7,000 of British troops.<sup id="cite_ref-91" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-91">[91]</a></sup> Ultimately, however, Charles Stuart and his uprising were defeated on 27 April 1746 at the <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Culloden" title="Battle of Culloden">Battle of Culloden</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-92" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-92">[92]</a></sup></p>
<p>The manoeuvres of the armies of both sides in the war on the upper Elbe occupied all the summer. Meanwhile, the political questions of the imperial election and of an understanding between Prussia and Britain were pending. The chief efforts of Austria were directed towards the valleys of the <a href="/wiki/Main_River" class="mw-redirect" title="Main River">Main</a> and of <a href="/wiki/Lahn" title="Lahn">Lahn</a> and <a href="/wiki/Frankfurt" title="Frankfurt">Frankfurt</a>, where the French and Austrian armies manoeuvred for a position from which to overawe the electoral body. Austrian Marshal <a href="/wiki/Otto_Ferdinand_von_Abensberg_und_Traun" title="Otto Ferdinand von Abensberg und Traun">Traun</a> was successful, and, as a result, Francis, the husband/consort of Maria Theresa was elected Holy Roman Emperor on 13 September 1745. Frederick agreed with Britain to recognise the election a few days later, but Maria Theresa would not conform to the Treaty of Breslau of 1741, by which she had been forced to recognise Frederick's annexation of Silesia. Maria Theresa now tried a further appeal to the fortunes of war to get Silesia back. Saxony joined Austria in this last attempt to reconquer Silesia.</p>
<p>In May 1745, The main Prussian army was stationed at <a href="/wiki/Z%C4%85bkowice_%C5%9Al%C4%85skie" title="Ząbkowice Śląskie">Frankenstein</a>. This army consisted of 59,000 soldiers and was fitted with 54 heavy cannon.<sup id="cite_ref-93" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-93">[93]</a></sup> Frederick learned that a combined Austrian-Saxon army of about 70,000 troops under the command of Prince Charles, was on the march to the northeast towards <a href="/wiki/Landeshut" class="mw-redirect" title="Landeshut">Landeshut</a>. To meet this threat to Silesia, Frederick II marched north toward <a href="/wiki/Reichenbach_im_Eulengebirge" class="mw-redirect" title="Reichenbach im Eulengebirge">Reichenbach</a>. Before he reached Reichenbach, Frederick learned that Prince Charles was crossing the mountains from the west to the east side and that Prince Charles planned to occupy the town of <a href="/wiki/Hohenfriedberg" class="mw-redirect" title="Hohenfriedberg">Hohenfriedberg</a>. Accordingly, Frederick encamped his army at <a href="/wiki/%C5%9Awidnica" title="Świdnica">Schweidwitz</a> and waited for Prince Charles to come to him. At this site, Frederick laid a trap for the superior Austrian-Saxon forces. Indeed, Frederick was operating on the theory that "to catch a mouse, leave the trap open."<sup id="cite_ref-94" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-94">[94]</a></sup> At 6:30 AM on 4 June 1745, while the Austrian-Saxon troops were still recovering from their long march, the trap was sprung on them in the <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Hohenfriedberg" title="Battle of Hohenfriedberg">Battle of Hohenfriedberg</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-95" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-95">[95]</a></sup> The Austrian-Saxon forces were no match for Frederick's army and especially his cavalry, and they lost half their artillery and almost a quarter of their men. At 9:00 AM, Prince Charles ordered a full retreat back toward Reichenberg.</p>
<p>A new advance of Prince Charles quickly brought on the <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Soor" title="Battle of Soor">Battle of Soor</a> on 30 September 1745. This battle was fought on ground destined to be famous in the <a href="/wiki/Austro-Prussian_War" title="Austro-Prussian War">war of 1866</a>. Frederick commanded an army that at this time numbered only 20,000 soldiers in the vicinity of Soor. He was facing Prince Charles with an army of 41,000 troops.<sup id="cite_ref-96" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-96">[96]</a></sup> At first in a position of great peril, but his army changed front in the face of the advancing enemy and by its boldness and tenacity won a remarkable victory on 30 September 1745 at <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Soor" title="Battle of Soor">Soor</a>.</p>
<p>But the campaign was not ended. An Austrian contingent from the Main joined the Saxons under Field Marshal <a href="/wiki/Frederick_Augustus_Rutowsky" title="Frederick Augustus Rutowsky">Rutowsky</a> (1702–1764), and a combined movement was made in the direction of Berlin by Rutowsky from Saxony and Prince Charles from Bohemia. The danger was very great. Frederick hurried up his forces from Silesia and marched as rapidly as possible on <a href="/wiki/Dresden" title="Dresden">Dresden</a>, in Saxony. Frederick won the actions of <a href="/wiki/Katholisch-Hennersdorf" class="mw-redirect" title="Katholisch-Hennersdorf">Katholisch-Hennersdorf</a> on 24 November 1745 and <a href="/wiki/G%C3%B6rlitz" title="Görlitz">Görlitz</a> on 25 November. Prince Charles was thereby forced to abandon his plans to attack Silesia and hurry back to defend Saxony. A second Prussian army under the <a href="/wiki/Leopold_I,_Prince_of_Anhalt-Dessau" title="Leopold I, Prince of Anhalt-Dessau">Old Dessauer</a> advanced up the Elbe from <a href="/wiki/Magdeburg" title="Magdeburg">Magdeburg</a> to meet Rutowsky. The latter took up a strong position at <a href="/wiki/Kesselsdorf" title="Kesselsdorf">Kesselsdorf</a> between <a href="/wiki/Meissen" title="Meissen">Meissen</a> and <a href="/wiki/Dresden" title="Dresden">Dresden</a>, but the veteran Leopold attacked him directly and without hesitation on 14 December 1745. The Saxons and their allies were completely <a href="/wiki/Rout" title="Rout">routed</a> after a hard struggle in the <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Kesselsdorf" title="Battle of Kesselsdorf">Battle of Kesselsdorf</a>. Maria Theresa was, at last, forced to give way. In the <a href="/wiki/Treaty_of_Dresden" title="Treaty of Dresden">Peace of Dresden</a> signed on 25 December 1745, she recognised Frederick's annexation of Silesia, as first recognised in the Peace of Breslau in 1741. Frederick on the other hand recognised the election of Maria Theresa's husband/consort—Francis I—as the Holy Roman Emperor.</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Italian_Campaigns_1741.E2.80.9347">Italian Campaigns 1741–47</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=War_of_the_Austrian_Succession&amp;action=edit&amp;section=9" title="Edit section: Italian Campaigns 1741–47">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:302px;"><a href="/wiki/File:La_familia_de_Felipe_V_(Van_Loo).jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c1/La_familia_de_Felipe_V_%28Van_Loo%29.jpg/300px-La_familia_de_Felipe_V_%28Van_Loo%29.jpg" width="300" height="239" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c1/La_familia_de_Felipe_V_%28Van_Loo%29.jpg/450px-La_familia_de_Felipe_V_%28Van_Loo%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c1/La_familia_de_Felipe_V_%28Van_Loo%29.jpg/600px-La_familia_de_Felipe_V_%28Van_Loo%29.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2717" data-file-height="2161" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:La_familia_de_Felipe_V_(Van_Loo).jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
<a href="/wiki/Philip_V_of_Spain" title="Philip V of Spain">Philip V of Spain</a>'s family by <a href="/wiki/Louis-Michel_van_Loo" title="Louis-Michel van Loo">Louis-Michel van Loo</a>.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>In central <a href="/wiki/Italy" title="Italy">Italy</a> an army of Spaniards and <a href="/wiki/Naples" title="Naples">Neapolitans</a> was collected for the purpose of conquering the <a href="/wiki/Milan" title="Milan">Milanese</a>. In 1741, the allied army of 40,000 Spaniards and Neapolitans under the command of the <a href="/wiki/Jos%C3%A9_Carrillo_de_Albornoz,_1st_Duke_of_Montemar" title="José Carrillo de Albornoz, 1st Duke of Montemar">Duke of Montmar</a> had advanced towards <a href="/wiki/Modena" title="Modena">Modena</a>, the Duke of Modena had allied himself with them, but the vigilant Austrian commander, Count <a href="/wiki/Otto_Ferdinand_von_Abensberg_und_Traun" title="Otto Ferdinand von Abensberg und Traun">Otto Ferdinand von Traun</a> had out-marched them, captured Modena and forced the Duke to make a separate peace.</p>
<p>The aggressiveness of the Spanish in Italy forced Empress Maria Theresa of Austria and King <a href="/wiki/Charles_Emmanuel_III_of_Sardinia" title="Charles Emmanuel III of Sardinia">Charles Emmanuel</a> of Sardinia into negotiations in early 1742.<sup id="cite_ref-97" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-97">[97]</a></sup> These negotiations were held at Turin. Maria Theresa sent her envoy <a href="/w/index.php?title=Count_Schulenburg&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Count Schulenburg (page does not exist)">Count Schulenburg</a> and King Charles Emmanuel sent the <a href="/wiki/Carlo_Vincenzo_Ferrero_d%27Ormea" title="Carlo Vincenzo Ferrero d'Ormea">Marquis d'Ormea</a>. On 1 February 1742, Schulenburg and Ormea signed the <a href="/wiki/Convention_of_Turin" title="Convention of Turin">Convention of Turin</a> which resolved (or postponed resolution) many differences and formed an alliance between the two countries.<sup id="cite_ref-98" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-98">[98]</a></sup> In 1742, field marshal Count Traun held his own with ease against the Spanish and Neapolitans. On 19 August 1742, Naples was forced by the arrival of a British naval squadron in Naple's own harbour, to withdraw her 10,000 troops from the Montemar force to provide for home defence.<sup id="cite_ref-99" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-99">[99]</a></sup> The Spanish force under Montemar was now too weak to advance in the <a href="/wiki/Po_Valley" title="Po Valley">Po Valley</a> and a second Spanish army was sent to Italy via France. Sardinia had allied herself with Austria in the <a href="/wiki/Convention_of_Turin" title="Convention of Turin">Convention of Turin</a> and at the same time neither state was at war with France and this led to curious complications, combats being fought in the <a href="/wiki/Is%C3%A8re_(river)" title="Isère (river)">Isère</a> valley between the troops of Sardinia and of Spain, in which the French took no part. At the end of 1742, the Duke of Montemar was replaced as head of the Spanish forces in Italy by <a href="/wiki/Jean_Thierry_du_Mont,_comte_de_Gages" title="Jean Thierry du Mont, comte de Gages">Count Gages</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-100" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-100">[100]</a></sup></p>
<p>In 1743, the Spanish on the <a href="/wiki/Panaro_(river)" title="Panaro (river)">Panaro</a> had achieved a victory over Traun at <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Campo_Santo" title="Battle of Campo Santo">Campo Santo</a> on 8 February 1743.<sup id="cite_ref-101" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-101">[101]</a></sup> However, the next six months were wasted in inaction and <a href="/wiki/Georg_Christian,_F%C3%BCrst_von_Lobkowitz" title="Georg Christian, Fürst von Lobkowitz">Georg Christian, Fürst von Lobkowitz</a>, joining Traun with reinforcements from Germany, drove back the Spanish to <a href="/wiki/Rimini" title="Rimini">Rimini</a>. Observing from <a href="/wiki/Venice" title="Venice">Venice</a>, <a href="/wiki/Jean-Jacques_Rousseau" title="Jean-Jacques Rousseau">Rousseau</a> hailed the Spanish retreat as "the finest military manoeuvre of the whole century."<sup id="cite_ref-Cranston183_102-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Cranston183-102">[102]</a></sup> The Spanish-<a href="/wiki/Savoy" title="Savoy">Savoyan</a> War in the <a href="/wiki/Alps" title="Alps">Alps</a> continued without much result, the only incident of note being the first Battle of Casteldelfino (7–10 October 1743), when an initial French offensive was beaten off.</p>
<p>In 1744 the Italian war became serious. Prior to the <a href="/wiki/War_of_the_Spanish_Succession" title="War of the Spanish Succession">War of the Spanish Succession</a> (1701–1714) Spain and Austria had been ruled by the same (<a href="/wiki/Habsburg" class="mw-redirect" title="Habsburg">Habsburg</a>) royal house. Consequently, the foreign policies of Austria and Spain in regards to Italy had a symmetry of interests and these interests were usually opposed to the interests of <a href="/wiki/House_of_Bourbon" title="House of Bourbon">Bourbon</a> controlled France.<sup id="cite_ref-103" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-103">[103]</a></sup> However, since the <a href="/wiki/Treaty_of_Utrecht" title="Treaty of Utrecht">Treaty of Utrecht</a> and the end of the War of the Spanish Succession, the childless last Habsburg monarch (<a href="/wiki/Charles_II_of_Spain" title="Charles II of Spain">Charles II</a>) had been replaced by the Bourbon grandson of the French king Louis XIV <a href="/wiki/Philip_V_of_Spain" title="Philip V of Spain">Philip of Anjou</a>, who became Philip V in Spain. Now the symmetry of foreign policy interests in regards to Italy existed between Bourbon France and Bourbon Spain with Habsburg Austria usually in opposition.<sup id="cite_ref-104" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-104">[104]</a></sup> King <a href="/wiki/Charles_Emmanuel_III_of_Sardinia" title="Charles Emmanuel III of Sardinia">Charles Emmanuel</a> of Savoy had followed the long-established foreign policy of Savoy of opposing Spanish interference in northern Italy.<sup id="cite_ref-Smith-p243_58-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Smith-p243-58">[58]</a></sup> Now in 1744, Savoy was faced with a grandiose military plan of the combined Spanish and French armies (called the <a href="/wiki/Gallispan" class="mw-redirect" title="Gallispan">Gallispan</a> army) for conquest of northern Italy.</p>
<p>However, in implementing this plan, the Gallispan generals at the front were hampered by the orders of their respective governments. For example, the commander of the Spanish army in the field, the <a href="/wiki/Louis_Fran%C3%A7ois,_Prince_of_Conti" title="Louis François, Prince of Conti">Prince of Conti</a>, could not get along with, or even reason with, the <a href="/wiki/Jaime_Miguel_de_Guzm%C3%A1n_de_Avalos_y_Spinola" class="mw-redirect" title="Jaime Miguel de Guzmán de Avalos y Spinola">Marquis de La Mina</a>, the Supreme commander of all Spanish forces.<sup id="cite_ref-Browning-p166_105-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Browning-p166-105">[105]</a></sup> The Prince of Conti felt that the Marquis "deferred blindly to all orders coming from Spain" without any consideration of the realities on the ground.<sup id="cite_ref-Browning-p166_105-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Browning-p166-105">[105]</a></sup> In preparation for the military campaign the Gallispan forces sought to cross the Alps in June 1744 and regroup the army in <a href="/wiki/Dauphin%C3%A9" title="Dauphiné">Dauphiné</a> uniting there with the army on the lower Po.<sup id="cite_ref-106" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-106">[106]</a></sup></p>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Retrato_de_Carlos_III_de_Espa%C3%B1a.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/39/Retrato_de_Carlos_III_de_Espa%C3%B1a.jpg/220px-Retrato_de_Carlos_III_de_Espa%C3%B1a.jpg" width="220" height="294" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/39/Retrato_de_Carlos_III_de_Espa%C3%B1a.jpg/330px-Retrato_de_Carlos_III_de_Espa%C3%B1a.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/39/Retrato_de_Carlos_III_de_Espa%C3%B1a.jpg/440px-Retrato_de_Carlos_III_de_Espa%C3%B1a.jpg 2x" data-file-width="640" data-file-height="856" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Retrato_de_Carlos_III_de_Espa%C3%B1a.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
<a href="/wiki/Charles_III_of_Spain" title="Charles III of Spain">Charles III of Spain</a> by <a href="/wiki/Anton_Raphael_Mengs" title="Anton Raphael Mengs">Anton Raphael Mengs</a>.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>The support of <a href="/wiki/Genoa" title="Genoa">Genoa</a> allowed a road into central Italy.<sup id="cite_ref-Browning-p166_105-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Browning-p166-105">[105]</a></sup> While the Prince of Conti stayed in the north, Count <a href="/wiki/Jean_Bonaventure_du_Mont,_comte_de_Gages" class="mw-redirect" title="Jean Bonaventure du Mont, comte de Gages">Gages</a> followed this road to the south. But then the Austrian commander, Prince Lobkowitz took the offensive and drove the Spanish army of the <a href="/wiki/Jean_Bonaventure_du_Mont,_comte_de_Gages" class="mw-redirect" title="Jean Bonaventure du Mont, comte de Gages">Count de Gages</a> further southward towards the Neapolitan frontier near the small town of <a href="/wiki/Velletri" title="Velletri">Velletri</a>. Velletri just happened to be the birthplace of <a href="/wiki/Caesar_Augustus" class="mw-redirect" title="Caesar Augustus">Caesar Augustus</a>, but now from June through August 1744, Velletri became the scene of extensive military maneuvering between the French-Spanish army under the command of the Count Gages and the Austrian forces under the command of Prince Lobkowitz<sup id="cite_ref-107" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-107">[107]</a></sup> The King of Naples (the future <a href="/wiki/Charles_III_of_Spain" title="Charles III of Spain">Charles III of Spain</a>) was increasingly worried about the Austrian army operating so close to his borders and decided to assist the Spaniards. Together a combined army of French, Spanish and Neapolitans surprised the Austrian army on the night of 16–17 June 1744. The Austrians were routed from three important hills around the town of Velletri during the attack.<sup id="cite_ref-Browning-p164_108-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Browning-p164-108">[108]</a></sup> This battle is sometimes called the "Battle of Nemi" after the small town of Nemi located nearby. Because of this surprise attack, the combined army was able to take possession of the town of Velletri. Thus, the surprise attack has also been called the "first <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Velletri_(1744)" title="Battle of Velletri (1744)">Battle of Velletri</a>."</p>
<p>In early August 1744, the King of Naples paid a visit in person to the newly captured town of Velletri.<sup id="cite_ref-Browning-p164_108-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Browning-p164-108">[108]</a></sup> Hearing about the presence of the King, the Austrians developed a plan for a daring raid on Velletri. During the predawn hours of 11 August 1744, about 6,000 Austrians under the direct command of <a href="/wiki/Maximilian_Ulysses_Browne" title="Maximilian Ulysses Browne">Count Browne</a> staged a surprise raid on the town of Velletri. They were attempting to abduct the King of Naples during his stay in the town. However, after occupying Velletri and searching the entire town, the Austrians found no hint of the King of Naples. The King had become aware of what was happening and had fled through a window of the palace where he was staying and rode off half-dressed on horseback out of the town.<sup id="cite_ref-109" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-109">[109]</a></sup> This was the second <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Velletri_(1744)" title="Battle of Velletri (1744)">Battle of Velletri</a>. The failure of the raid on Velletri meant that the Austrian march toward Naples was over. The defeated Austrians were ordered north where they could be used in the Piedmont of northern Italy to assist the King of Sardinia against the Prince of Conti. Count de Gages followed the Austrians north with a weak force. Meanwhile, the King of Naples returned home.</p>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Louis_15.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fc/Louis_15.jpg/220px-Louis_15.jpg" width="220" height="288" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fc/Louis_15.jpg/330px-Louis_15.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fc/Louis_15.jpg/440px-Louis_15.jpg 2x" data-file-width="800" data-file-height="1046" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Louis_15.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
The <a href="/wiki/Louis_Fran%C3%A7ois,_Prince_of_Conti" title="Louis François, Prince of Conti">Prince of Conti</a> by Alexis Simon Belle.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>The war in the Alps and the <a href="/wiki/Apennine_Mountains" title="Apennine Mountains">Apennines</a> had already been keenly contested before the Prince of Conti and the Gallispan army had come down out of the Alps. <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Villafranca_(1744)" title="Battle of Villafranca (1744)">Villefranche</a> and <a href="/wiki/Montalb%C3%A1n" title="Montalbán">Montalbán</a> had been stormed by Conti on 20 April 1744. After coming down out of the Alps, Prince Conti began his advance into Piedmont on 5 July 1744.<sup id="cite_ref-110" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-110">[110]</a></sup> On 19 July 1744, the Gallispan army engaged the Sardinian army in some desperate fighting at <a href="/wiki/Peyre-Longue" class="mw-redirect" title="Peyre-Longue">Peyre-Longue</a> on 18 July 1744.<sup id="cite_ref-111" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-111">[111]</a></sup> As a result of the battle, the Gallispan army took control of <a href="/wiki/Casteldelfino" title="Casteldelfino">Casteldelfino</a> in the second <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Casteldelfino" title="Battle of Casteldelfino">Battle of Casteldelfino</a>. Conti then moved on to <a href="/wiki/Delmonte" class="mw-redirect" title="Delmonte">Delmonte</a> where on the night of 8–9 August 1744, (a mere 36 hours before the Spanish army in south of Italy fought the second Battle of Velletri, [as noted above]) the Gallispan army took the city of Delmonte from the Sardinians in the <a href="/w/index.php?title=Battle_of_Delmonte&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Battle of Delmonte (page does not exist)">Battle of Delmonte</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-112" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-112">[112]</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Charles_Emmanuel_III_of_Sardinia" title="Charles Emmanuel III of Sardinia">King of Sardinia</a> was defeated yet again by Conti in a great Battle at <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Madonna_dell%27Olmo" title="Battle of Madonna dell'Olmo">Madonna dell'Olmo</a> on 30 September 1744 near Coni (<a href="/wiki/Cuneo" title="Cuneo">Cuneo</a>).<sup id="cite_ref-113" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-113">[113]</a></sup> Conti did not, however, succeed in taking the huge fortress at Coni and had to retire into Dauphiné for his winter quarters. Thus, the Gallispan army never did combine with the Spanish army under Count of Gages in the south and now the Austro-Sardinian army lay between them.</p>
<p>The campaign in Italy in 1745 was also no mere war of posts. The Convention of Turin of February 1742 (described above), which established a provisional relationship between Austria and Sardinia had caused some consternation in the <a href="/wiki/Republic_of_Genoa" title="Republic of Genoa">Republic of Genoa</a>. However, when this provisional relationship was given a more durable and reliable character in the signing of the <a href="/wiki/Treaty_of_Worms_(1743)" title="Treaty of Worms (1743)">Treaty of Worms (1743)</a> signed on 13 September 1743,<sup id="cite_ref-114" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-114">[114]</a></sup> the government of Genoa became fearful. This fear of diplomatic isolation had caused the Genoese Republic to abandon its neutrality in the war and join the Bourbon cause.<sup id="cite_ref-Browning-p205_115-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Browning-p205-115">[115]</a></sup> Consequently, the Genoese Republic signed a secret treaty with the Bourbon allies of France, Spain and Naples. On 26 June 1745, Genoa declared war on Sardinia.<sup id="cite_ref-Browning-p205_115-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Browning-p205-115">[115]</a></sup></p>
<p>Empress Maria Theresa, was frustrated with the failure of Lobkowitz to stop the advance of Gage. Accordingly, Lobkowitz was replaced with Count Schulenburg.<sup id="cite_ref-116" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-116">[116]</a></sup> A change in the command of the Austrians, encouraged the Bourbon allies to strike first in the spring of 1745. Accordingly, Count de Gages moved from Modena towards <a href="/wiki/Lucca" title="Lucca">Lucca</a>, the Gallispan army in the Alps under the new command of <a href="/wiki/Jean-Baptiste_Francois_des_Marets,_marquis_de_Maillebois" title="Jean-Baptiste Francois des Marets, marquis de Maillebois">Marshal Maillebois</a> (Prince Conti and Marshal Maillebois had exchanged commands over the winter of 1744–1745<sup id="cite_ref-117" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-117">[117]</a></sup>) advanced through the <a href="/wiki/Italian_Riviera" title="Italian Riviera">Italian Riviera</a> to the <a href="/wiki/Tanaro" title="Tanaro">Tanaro</a>. In the middle of July 1745, the two armies were at last concentrated between the <a href="/wiki/Scrivia" title="Scrivia">Scrivia</a> and the Tanaro. Together Count de Gage's army and the Gallispan army composed an unusually large number of 80,000 men. A swift march on <a href="/wiki/Piacenza" title="Piacenza">Piacenza</a> drew the Austrian commander thither and in his absence the allies fell upon and completely defeated the Sardinians at <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Bassignano" title="Battle of Bassignano">Bassignano</a> on 27 September 1745, a victory which was quickly followed by the capture of <a href="/wiki/Alessandria" title="Alessandria">Alessandria</a>, <a href="/wiki/Valenza" title="Valenza">Valenza</a> and <a href="/wiki/Casale_Monferrato" title="Casale Monferrato">Casale Monferrato</a>. <a href="/wiki/Antoine-Henri_Jomini" title="Antoine-Henri Jomini">Jomini</a> calls the concentration of forces which effected the victory <i>"Le plus remarquable de toute la Guerre".</i></p>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Felipe_de_Parma.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/57/Felipe_de_Parma.jpg/220px-Felipe_de_Parma.jpg" width="220" height="306" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/57/Felipe_de_Parma.jpg/330px-Felipe_de_Parma.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/57/Felipe_de_Parma.jpg/440px-Felipe_de_Parma.jpg 2x" data-file-width="613" data-file-height="853" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Felipe_de_Parma.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
<a href="/wiki/Philip,_Duke_of_Parma" title="Philip, Duke of Parma">Infante Philip of Spain</a> by Laurent Pécheux.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>The complicated politics of Italy, however, is reflected in the fact that Count Maillebois was ultimately unable to turn his victory to account. Indeed, early in 1746, Austrian troops, freed by the Austrian peace with Frederick II of Prussia, passed through the <a href="/wiki/German_Tyrol" title="German Tyrol">Tyrol</a> into Italy. The Gallispan winter quarters at <a href="/wiki/Asti" title="Asti">Asti</a>, Italy, were brusquely attacked and a French garrison of 6,000 men at Asti was forced to capitulate.<sup id="cite_ref-118" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-118">[118]</a></sup> At the same time, <a href="/wiki/Maximilian_Ulysses_Browne" title="Maximilian Ulysses Browne">Maximilian Ulysses Count Browne</a> with an Austrian corps struck at the allies on the Lower Po, and cut off their communication with the main body of the Gallispan army in Piedmont. A series of minor actions thus completely destroyed the great concentration of Gallispan troops and the Austrians reconquered the duchy of Milan and took possession of much of northern Italy. The allies separated, Maillebois covering <a href="/wiki/Liguria" title="Liguria">Liguria</a>, the Spaniards marching against Browne. The latter was promptly and heavily reinforced and all that the Spaniards could do was to entrench themselves at Piacenza, <a href="/wiki/Duke_of_Parma" title="Duke of Parma">Philip, the Spanish Infante</a> as supreme commander calling up Maillebois to his aid. The French, skilfully conducted and marching rapidly, joined forces once more, but their situation was critical, for only two marches behind them the army of the King of Sardinia was in pursuit, and before them lay the principal army of the Austrians. The pitched <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Piacenza" title="Battle of Piacenza">Battle of Piacenza</a> on 16 June 1746 was hard fought but ended in an Austrian victory, with the Spanish army heavily mauled. That the army escaped at all was in the highest degree creditable to Maillebois and to his son and chief of staff. Under their leadership the Gallispan army eluded both the Austrians and the Sardinians and defeated an Austrian corps in the <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Rottofreddo" title="Battle of Rottofreddo">Battle of Rottofreddo</a> on 12 August 1746.<sup id="cite_ref-119" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-119">[119]</a></sup> Then the Austrian army made good its retreat back to Genoa.</p>
<p>Although the Austrian army was a mere shadow of its former self, when they returned to Genoa, the Austrians were soon in control of northern Italy. The Austrians occupied the <a href="/wiki/Republic_of_Genoa" title="Republic of Genoa">Republic of Genoa</a> on 6 September 1746.<sup id="cite_ref-120" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-120">[120]</a></sup> But they met with no success in their forays towards the Alps. Soon Genoa revolted from the oppressive rule of the victors, rose and drove out the Austrians on 5–11 December 1746. As an Allied invasion of <a href="/wiki/Provence" title="Provence">Provence</a> stalled, and the French, now commanded by <a href="/wiki/Charles_Louis_Auguste_Fouquet,_duc_de_Belle-Isle" title="Charles Louis Auguste Fouquet, duc de Belle-Isle">Charles Louis Auguste Fouquet, Duc de Belle-Isle</a>, took the offensive (1747).<sup id="cite_ref-121" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-121">[121]</a></sup> Genoa held out against a second Austrian siege.<sup id="cite_ref-122" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-122">[122]</a></sup> As usual the plan of campaign had been referred to Paris and Madrid. A picked corps of the French army under the <a href="/wiki/Louis_Charles_Armand_Fouquet" title="Louis Charles Armand Fouquet">Chevalier de Belle-Isle</a> (the younger brother of Marshal Belle-Isle<sup id="cite_ref-123" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-123">[123]</a></sup>) was ordered to storm the <a href="/wiki/Fort_of_Exilles" title="Fort of Exilles">fortified pass of Exilles</a> on 10 July 1747. However, the defending army of the Worms allies (Austria and Savoy) handed the French army a crushing defeat at this battle, which became known as the (<a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Assietta" title="Battle of Assietta">Colle dell'Assietta</a>).<sup id="cite_ref-Browning312_124-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Browning312-124">[124]</a></sup> At this battle, the chevalier, and with him much of the elite of the French nobility, were killed on the barricades.&lt;/ref name=Browning312&gt; Desultory campaigns continued between the Worms allies and the French until the conclusion of peace at <a href="/wiki/Treaty_of_Aix-la-Chapelle_(1748)" title="Treaty of Aix-la-Chapelle (1748)">Aix-la-Chapelle</a>.</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Later_campaigns">Later campaigns</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=War_of_the_Austrian_Succession&amp;action=edit&amp;section=10" title="Edit section: Later campaigns">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Low_Countries_1740.png" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/ab/Low_Countries_1740.png/220px-Low_Countries_1740.png" width="220" height="156" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/ab/Low_Countries_1740.png/330px-Low_Countries_1740.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/ab/Low_Countries_1740.png/440px-Low_Countries_1740.png 2x" data-file-width="813" data-file-height="575" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Low_Countries_1740.png" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Map of the Low Countries with <a href="/wiki/Bergen_op_Zoom" title="Bergen op Zoom">Bergen op Zoom</a> in the upper center.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>After Fontenoy, the French carried all before them. The withdrawal of most of the British forces to aid in suppressing the <a href="/wiki/Jacobite_rising_of_1745" title="Jacobite rising of 1745">Jacobite rising of 1745</a> at home left their allies in a helpless position. In 1746 the Dutch and the Austrians were driven back towards the line of the <a href="/wiki/Meuse_(river)" class="mw-redirect" title="Meuse (river)">Meuse</a>; the French took most of the important fortresses and in February 1746 <a href="/wiki/Siege_of_Brussels" title="Siege of Brussels">captured Brussels</a>. In September the British launched a <a href="/wiki/Raid_on_Lorient" title="Raid on Lorient">raid on Lorient</a> (in southern Brittany) in an attempt to divert French forces away from the Netherlands. The <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Roucoux" class="mw-redirect" title="Battle of Roucoux">Battle of Roucoux</a> (or Raucourt) near <a href="/wiki/Li%C3%A8ge_(city)" class="mw-redirect" title="Liège (city)">Liège</a>, fought on 11 October between the allies under Prince Charles of Lorraine and the French under Saxe, resulted in a victory for the latter. The <a href="/wiki/Dutch_Republic" title="Dutch Republic">Dutch Republic</a> itself was now in danger, and when in April 1747 Saxe's army, which had now conquered the Austrian Netherlands up to the Meuse, turned its attention to the <a href="/wiki/Dutch_Republic" title="Dutch Republic">United Provinces</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Barrier_Fortresses" class="mw-redirect" title="Barrier Fortresses">old fortresses on the frontier</a> offered but slight resistance. Since August 1746, ongoing talks at the <a href="/wiki/Congress_of_Breda" title="Congress of Breda">Congress of Breda</a> had discussed peace terms, but up to this point they had met with little success.</p>
<p>The Prince of Orange <a href="/wiki/William_IV,_Prince_of_Orange" title="William IV, Prince of Orange">William IV</a> and the Duke of Cumberland suffered a severe defeat at <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Lauffeld" title="Battle of Lauffeld">Lauffeld</a> (Lawfeld, also called Val) near Maastricht on 2 July 1747, and Saxe, after his victory, promptly and secretly despatched a corps under Marshal <a href="/wiki/Ulrich_Friedrich_Waldemar_von_L%C3%B6wendahl_(Comte_de_Lowendahl)" class="mw-redirect" title="Ulrich Friedrich Waldemar von Löwendahl (Comte de Lowendahl)">Lowendahl</a> to <a href="/wiki/Siege_of_Bergen_op_Zoom_(1747)" title="Siege of Bergen op Zoom (1747)">besiege Bergen op Zoom</a> in northern Brabant. On 18 September the French stormed Bergen op Zoom, and in the last year of the war <a href="/wiki/Maastricht" title="Maastricht">Maastricht</a>, attacked by the entire forces of Saxe and Lowendahl, <a href="/wiki/Siege_of_Maastricht_(1748)" title="Siege of Maastricht (1748)">surrendered on 7 May 1748</a>. A large Russian army arrived to join the allies, but too late to be of use. Russia and Sweden had settled their differences in the <a href="/wiki/Peace_of_%C3%85bo" class="mw-redirect" title="Peace of Åbo">Peace of Åbo</a> in 1743, and in 1746 Russia had allied itself with Austria. Eventually, <a href="/wiki/30,000_Russians" class="mw-redirect" title="30,000 Russians">30,000 Russians</a><span class="noprint" style="font-size:85%; font-style: normal;">&#160;(<a href="https://ru.wikipedia.org/wiki/%D0%A0%D0%B5%D0%B9%D0%BD%D1%81%D0%BA%D0%B8%D0%B9_%D0%BF%D0%BE%D1%85%D0%BE%D0%B4_(1748)" class="extiw" title="ru:Рейнский поход (1748)">ru</a>)</span> marched from <a href="/wiki/Livonia" title="Livonia">Livonia</a> to the Rhine, an event not without military significance, and in a manner prefiguring the great invasions of 1813–1814 and 1945. The major powers signed the general Peace of Aix-la-Chapelle (<a href="/wiki/Aachen" title="Aachen">Aachen</a>) on 18 October 1748.</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Conclusion_of_the_war">Conclusion of the war</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=War_of_the_Austrian_Succession&amp;action=edit&amp;section=11" title="Edit section: Conclusion of the war">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:302px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Europe_1748-1766_en.png" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/bf/Europe_1748-1766_en.png/300px-Europe_1748-1766_en.png" width="300" height="214" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/bf/Europe_1748-1766_en.png/450px-Europe_1748-1766_en.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/bf/Europe_1748-1766_en.png/600px-Europe_1748-1766_en.png 2x" data-file-width="3872" data-file-height="2761" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Europe_1748-1766_en.png" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Europe in the years after the Treaty of Aix-la-Chapelle in 1748.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>The War of Austrian Succession concluded with the <a href="/wiki/Treaty_of_Aix-la-Chapelle_(1748)" title="Treaty of Aix-la-Chapelle (1748)">Treaty of Aix-la-Chapelle (1748)</a>. Maria Theresa and Austria survived nearly <i><a href="/wiki/Status_quo_ante_bellum" title="Status quo ante bellum">status quo ante bellum</a></i>, sacrificing only the territory of Silesia, which Austria conceded to Prussia, and a few minor territorial losses to Spain in northern Italy. The loss of Silesia was, in great measure, a humiliating defeat for Austria's leadership of the German states within the Holy Roman Empire. This marked the beginning of the <a href="/wiki/German_dualism" class="mw-redirect" title="German dualism">German dualism</a> between Prussia and Austria, which would ultimately fuel German nationalism and the drive to unify Germany as a single entity.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (August 2012)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup></p>
<p>Despite his victories, Louis XV of France, who wanted to appear as an arbiter and statesman and not as a conqueror, gave all of his conquests back to his defeated enemies with honour, arguing that he was "King of France, not a merchant".<sup id="cite_ref-125" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-125">[125]</a></sup> This decision, largely misunderstood by his generals and by the French people, made the king unpopular at home. The French obtained so little of what they had fought for that they adopted the expressions <i>Bête comme la paix</i> ("Stupid as the peace") and <i>Travailler pour le roi de Prusse</i> ("To work for the king of Prussia", i.e. working for nothing). France definitely succeeded in humiliating Maria Theresa and her kingdom. But because of this France had bolstered Prussia's power which was to continue to grow, to France's later detriment. Twice during the war, Prussia had made peace with Austria without informing France, leading Louis XV to consider Frederick II of Prussia (whom he already greatly disliked) an untrustworthy ally. Despite the long history of conflict between the Houses of Habsburg and Bourbon, he began to make overtures of alliance to Austria instead.</p>
<p>Spain, in one way or another, managed to achieve some of her war aims, which mostly centred on an effort to reinstate Spanish influence in the Italian peninsula.</p>
<p>Britain managed to get out of the war with a favorable settlement and on its own terms, which angered the Austrians; Britain's power was increasing and its interests becoming even more complex. Realizing that Austria was no longer the sole hegemon of Central Europe, Britain decided to <a href="/wiki/Anglo-Prussian_alliance_(1756)" title="Anglo-Prussian alliance (1756)">align itself with Prussia</a> in order to protect Hanover from future French attack. This alliance however ended up destabilizing the continent, as the other great powers braced themselves with a counter grand alliance for an <a href="/wiki/Seven_Years%27_War" title="Seven Years' War">upcoming war</a> that proved to be even grander in scale.</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="General_character_of_the_war_in_Europe">General character of the war in Europe</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=War_of_the_Austrian_Succession&amp;action=edit&amp;section=12" title="Edit section: General character of the war in Europe">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>The triumph of Prussia was in a great measure due to its fuller application of principles of tactics and discipline universally recognised though less universally enforced. The other powers reorganised their forces after the war, not so much on the Prussian model as on the basis of a stricter application of known general principles. Prussia, moreover, was far ahead of all the other continental powers in administration, and over Austria, in particular, its advantage in this matter was almost decisive. Added to this was the personal ascendancy of Frederick, as opposed to generals who were responsible for their men to their individual sovereigns.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (August 2012)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup></p>
<p>The war, like other conflicts of the time, featured an extraordinary disparity between the end and the means. The political schemes to be executed by the French and other armies were as grandiose as any of modern times. Their execution, under the conditions of time and space, invariably fell short of expectations, and the history of the war proves, as that of the <a href="/wiki/Seven_Years%27_War" title="Seven Years' War">Seven Years' War</a> was to prove, that the small standing army of the 18th century could conquer by degrees, but could not deliver a decisive blow. Frederick alone, with a definite end and proportionate means to achieve it, succeeded. Less was to be expected when the armies were composed of allied contingents, sent to the war each for a different object. The allied national armies of 1813 (at the <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Leipzig" title="Battle of Leipzig">Battle of Leipzig</a>) co-operated loyally, for they had much at stake and worked for a common object. Those of 1741 represented the divergent private interests of the several dynasties, and achieved nothing.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (August 2012)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup></p>
<ul>
<li>Further Reading: <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://www.poetry-archive.com/v/to_the_queen_of_hungary.html">"To the Queen of Hungary"</a> is a poem by <a href="/wiki/Voltaire" title="Voltaire">Voltaire</a> which describes the character of the war from a largely French perspective.</li>
</ul>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="North_America">North America</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=War_of_the_Austrian_Succession&amp;action=edit&amp;section=13" title="Edit section: North America">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/King_George%27s_War" title="King George's War">King George's War</a></div>
<div role="navigation" class="navbox" aria-labelledby="King_George.27s_War" style="margin:0;float:right;clear:right;width:315px;margin-bottom:0.5em;margin-left:1em;;padding:3px">

<tr>
<td class="navbox-abovebelow" colspan="2" style="background-color:#DCDCDC;">
<div>Part of the <a class="mw-selflink selflink">War of the Austrian Succession</a></div>
</td>
</tr>
</table>
</div>
<p>The war was also conducted in North America and India. In North America the conflict was known in the <a href="/wiki/British_America" title="British America">British colonies</a> as <a href="/wiki/King_George%27s_War" title="King George's War">King George's War</a>, and did not begin until after formal war declarations of France and Britain reached the colonies in May 1744. The frontiers between <a href="/wiki/New_France" title="New France">New France</a> and the British colonies of <a href="/wiki/New_England" title="New England">New England</a>, <a href="/wiki/Province_of_New_York" title="Province of New York">New York</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Nova_Scotia" title="Nova Scotia">Nova Scotia</a> were the site of frequent small scale raids, primarily by French colonial troops and their Indian allies against British targets, although several attempts were made by British colonists to organise expeditions against New France. The most significant incident was <a href="/wiki/Siege_of_Louisbourg_(1745)" title="Siege of Louisbourg (1745)">the capture</a> of the French <a href="/wiki/Fortress_Louisbourg" class="mw-redirect" title="Fortress Louisbourg">Fortress Louisbourg</a> on <a href="/wiki/Cape_Breton_Island" title="Cape Breton Island">Cape Breton Island</a> (Île Royale) by an expedition (29 April – 16 June 1745) of colonial militia organised by <a href="/wiki/Province_of_Massachusetts_Bay" title="Province of Massachusetts Bay">Massachusetts</a> Governor <a href="/wiki/William_Shirley" title="William Shirley">William Shirley</a>, commanded by <a href="/wiki/William_Pepperrell" title="William Pepperrell">William Pepperrell</a> of <a href="/wiki/Maine" title="Maine">Maine</a> (then part of Massachusetts), and assisted by a Royal Navy fleet. <a href="/wiki/Duc_d%27Anville_Expedition" class="mw-redirect" title="Duc d'Anville Expedition">A French expedition</a> to recover Louisbourg in 1746 failed due to bad weather, disease, and the death of its commander. Louisbourg was returned to France in exchange for <a href="/wiki/Madras" class="mw-redirect" title="Madras">Madras</a>, generating much anger among the British colonists, who felt they had eliminated a nest of privateers with its capture.</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="India">India</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=War_of_the_Austrian_Succession&amp;action=edit&amp;section=14" title="Edit section: India">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Further information: <a href="/wiki/Carnatic_Wars" title="Carnatic Wars">Carnatic Wars</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:302px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Flag_of_the_British_East_India_Company_(1707).svg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b3/Flag_of_the_British_East_India_Company_%281707%29.svg/300px-Flag_of_the_British_East_India_Company_%281707%29.svg.png" width="300" height="177" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b3/Flag_of_the_British_East_India_Company_%281707%29.svg/450px-Flag_of_the_British_East_India_Company_%281707%29.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b3/Flag_of_the_British_East_India_Company_%281707%29.svg/600px-Flag_of_the_British_East_India_Company_%281707%29.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="1100" data-file-height="650" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Flag_of_the_British_East_India_Company_(1707).svg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Flag of the <a href="/wiki/East_India_Company" title="East India Company">East India Company</a> (founded in 1600)</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>The war marked the beginning of great power in England and the powerful struggle between <a href="/wiki/United_Kingdom" title="United Kingdom">Britain</a> and <a href="/wiki/France" title="France">France</a> in India and of European military ascendancy and political intervention in the subcontinent. Major hostilities began with the arrival of a naval squadron under <a href="/wiki/Bertrand-Fran%C3%A7ois_Mah%C3%A9_de_La_Bourdonnais" title="Bertrand-François Mahé de La Bourdonnais">Mahé de la Bourdonnais</a>, carrying troops from France. In September 1746 Bourdonnais landed his troops near <a href="/wiki/Chennai" title="Chennai">Madras</a> and laid siege to the port. Although it was the main British settlement in the <a href="/wiki/Carnatic_region" title="Carnatic region">Carnatic</a>, Madras was weakly fortified and had only a small garrison, reflecting the thoroughly commercial nature of the European presence in India hitherto. On 10 September, only six days after the arrival of the French force, Madras surrendered. The terms of the surrender agreed by Bourdonnais provided for the settlement to be ransomed back for a cash payment by the <a href="/wiki/British_East_India_Company" class="mw-redirect" title="British East India Company">British East India Company</a>. However, this concession was opposed by <a href="/wiki/Joseph_Fran%C3%A7ois_Dupleix" title="Joseph François Dupleix">Dupleix</a>, the governor general of the Indian possessions of the <a href="/wiki/French_East_India_Company" title="French East India Company">Compagnie des Indes</a>. When Bourdonnais was forced to leave India in October after the devastation of his squadron by a cyclone Dupleix reneged on the agreement. The <a href="/wiki/Nawab_of_the_Carnatic" class="mw-redirect" title="Nawab of the Carnatic">Nawab of the Carnatic</a> <a href="/wiki/Anwaruddin_Muhammed_Khan" class="mw-redirect" title="Anwaruddin Muhammed Khan">Anwaruddin Muhammed Khan</a> intervened in support of the British and advanced to retake Madras, but despite vast superiority in numbers his army was easily and bloodily crushed by the French, in the first demonstration of the gap in quality that had opened up between European and Indian armies.</p>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:252px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Bombardement_de_Pondichery_en_1748_par_la_flotte_anglaise.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a2/Bombardement_de_Pondichery_en_1748_par_la_flotte_anglaise.jpg/250px-Bombardement_de_Pondichery_en_1748_par_la_flotte_anglaise.jpg" width="250" height="154" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a2/Bombardement_de_Pondichery_en_1748_par_la_flotte_anglaise.jpg/375px-Bombardement_de_Pondichery_en_1748_par_la_flotte_anglaise.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a2/Bombardement_de_Pondichery_en_1748_par_la_flotte_anglaise.jpg/500px-Bombardement_de_Pondichery_en_1748_par_la_flotte_anglaise.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1613" data-file-height="991" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Bombardement_de_Pondichery_en_1748_par_la_flotte_anglaise.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
British Admiral Edward Boscawen <a href="/wiki/Siege_of_Pondicherry_(1748)" title="Siege of Pondicherry (1748)">besieged Pondicherry</a> in the later months of 1748</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>The French now turned to the remaining British settlement in the Carnatic, <a href="/wiki/Fort_St_David" class="mw-redirect" title="Fort St David">Fort St David</a> at <a href="/wiki/Cuddalore" title="Cuddalore">Cuddalore</a>, which was dangerously close to the main French settlement of <a href="/wiki/Pondicherry_district" class="mw-redirect" title="Pondicherry district">Pondichéry</a>. The first French force sent against Cuddalore was surprised and defeated nearby by the forces of the Nawab and the British garrison in December 1746. Early in 1747 a second expedition laid siege to Fort St David but withdrew on the arrival of a British naval squadron in March. A final attempt in June 1748 avoided the fort and attacked the weakly fortified town of Cuddalore itself, but was routed by the British garrison.</p>
<p>With the arrival of a naval squadron under <a href="/wiki/Edward_Boscawen" title="Edward Boscawen">Admiral Boscawen</a>, carrying troops and artillery, the British went on the offensive, laying siege to Pondichéry. They enjoyed a considerable superiority in numbers over the defenders, but the settlement had been heavily fortified by Dupleix and after two months the siege was abandoned.</p>
<p>The peace settlement brought the return of Madras to the British company, exchanged for Louisbourg in Canada. However, the conflict between the two companies continued by proxy during the interval before the outbreak of the <a href="/wiki/Seven_Years%27_War" title="Seven Years' War">Seven Years' War</a>, with British and French forces fighting on behalf of rival claimants to the thrones of Hyderabad and the <a href="/wiki/Nawab_of_the_Carnatic" class="mw-redirect" title="Nawab of the Carnatic">Carnatic</a>.</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Naval_operations">Naval operations</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=War_of_the_Austrian_Succession&amp;action=edit&amp;section=15" title="Edit section: Naval operations">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>The naval <a href="/wiki/Operation_(military)" class="mw-redirect" title="Operation (military)">operations</a> of this war were entangled with the <a href="/wiki/War_of_Jenkins%27_Ear" title="War of Jenkins' Ear">War of Jenkins' Ear</a>, which broke out in 1739 in consequence of the long disputes between Britain and Spain over their conflicting claims in America. The war was remarkable for the prominence of privateering on both sides. It was carried on by the Spaniards in the West Indies with great success, and actively at home. The French were no less active in all seas. Mahé de la Bourdonnais's attack on Madras partook largely of the nature of a privateering venture. The British retaliated with vigour. The total number of captures by French and Spanish <a href="/wiki/Privateer" title="Privateer">corsairs</a> was in all probability larger than the list of British – as the French wit <a href="/wiki/Voltaire" title="Voltaire">Voltaire</a> drolly put it upon hearing his government's boast, namely, that more British merchants were taken because there were many more British merchant ships to take; but partly also because the British government had not yet begun to enforce the use of <a href="/wiki/Convoy" title="Convoy">convoy</a> so strictly as it did in later times.</p>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Further information: <a href="/wiki/War_of_Jenkins%27_Ear" title="War of Jenkins' Ear">War of Jenkins' Ear</a></div>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="The_West_Indies">The West Indies</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=War_of_the_Austrian_Succession&amp;action=edit&amp;section=16" title="Edit section: The West Indies">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div role="navigation" class="navbox" aria-labelledby="War_of_Jenkins.27_Ear" style="margin:0;float:right;clear:right;width:315px;margin-bottom:0.5em;margin-left:1em;;padding:3px">
