<tr>
<td class="navbox-abovebelow" colspan="2" style="background-color:#DCDCDC;">
<div>Part of the <a class="mw-selflink selflink">War of the Austrian Succession</a></div>
</td>
</tr>
</table>
</div>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Edward_Vernon_by_Thomas_Gainsborough.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/38/Edward_Vernon_by_Thomas_Gainsborough.jpg/220px-Edward_Vernon_by_Thomas_Gainsborough.jpg" width="220" height="272" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/38/Edward_Vernon_by_Thomas_Gainsborough.jpg/330px-Edward_Vernon_by_Thomas_Gainsborough.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/38/Edward_Vernon_by_Thomas_Gainsborough.jpg/440px-Edward_Vernon_by_Thomas_Gainsborough.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2400" data-file-height="2966" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Edward_Vernon_by_Thomas_Gainsborough.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
<a href="/wiki/Vice-Admiral" class="mw-redirect" title="Vice-Admiral">Vice-Admiral</a> <a href="/wiki/Admiral_Vernon" class="mw-redirect" title="Admiral Vernon">Edward Vernon</a></div>
</div>
</div>
<p>War on Spain was declared by Great Britain on 23 October 1739, which has become known as the <a href="/wiki/War_of_Jenkins%27_Ear" title="War of Jenkins' Ear">War of Jenkins' Ear</a>. A plan was laid for combined operations against the Spanish colonies from east and west. One force, military and naval, was to assault them from the <a href="/wiki/West_Indies" title="West Indies">West Indies</a> under Admiral <a href="/wiki/Edward_Vernon" title="Edward Vernon">Edward Vernon</a>. Another, to be commanded by Commodore <a href="/wiki/George_Anson,_1st_Baron_Anson" title="George Anson, 1st Baron Anson">George Anson</a>, afterwards Lord Anson, was to round <a href="/wiki/Cape_Horn" title="Cape Horn">Cape Horn</a> and to fall upon the Pacific coast of Latin America. Delays, bad preparations, <a href="/wiki/Dockyard" class="mw-redirect" title="Dockyard">dockyard</a> corruption, and the squabbles of the naval and military officers concerned caused the failure of a hopeful scheme. On 21 November 1739, Admiral Vernon did, however, succeed in capturing the ill-defended Spanish harbour of <a href="/wiki/Porto_Bello,_Panama" class="mw-redirect" title="Porto Bello, Panama">Porto Bello</a> in present-day <a href="/wiki/Panama" title="Panama">Panama</a>. When Vernon had been joined by Sir <a href="/wiki/Chaloner_Ogle" title="Chaloner Ogle">Chaloner Ogle</a> with massive naval reinforcements and a strong body of troops, an attack was made on <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Cartagena_de_Indias" title="Battle of Cartagena de Indias">Cartagena</a> in what is now <a href="/wiki/Colombia" title="Colombia">Colombia</a> (9 March – 24 April 1741). The delay had given the Spanish under <a href="/wiki/Sebasti%C3%A1n_de_Eslava" title="Sebastián de Eslava">Sebastián de Eslava</a> and <a href="/wiki/Blas_de_Lezo" title="Blas de Lezo">Blas de Lezo</a> time to prepare. After two months of skilful defence by the Spanish, the British attack finally succumbed to a massive outbreak of disease and withdrew having suffered a dreadful loss of lives and ships.</p>
<p>The war in the West Indies, after two other unsuccessful attacks had been made on Spanish territory, died down and did not revive till 1748. The expedition under Anson sailed late, was very ill-provided, and less strong than had been intended. It consisted of six ships and left Britain on 18 September 1740. Anson returned alone with his <a href="/wiki/Flagship" title="Flagship">flagship</a> the <i><a href="/wiki/HMS_Centurion_(1732)" title="HMS Centurion (1732)">Centurion</a></i> on 15 June 1744. The other vessels had either failed to round the Horn or had been lost. But Anson had harried the coast of <a href="/wiki/Chile" title="Chile">Chile</a> and <a href="/wiki/Peru" title="Peru">Peru</a> and had captured a Spanish galleon of immense value near the <a href="/wiki/Philippines" title="Philippines">Philippines</a>. His cruise was a great feat of resolution and endurance.</p>
<p>After the failure of the British invasions and a Spanish <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Bloody_Marsh" title="Battle of Bloody Marsh">counter invasion</a> of <a href="/wiki/Province_of_Georgia" title="Province of Georgia">Georgia</a> in 1742, belligerent naval actions in the Caribbean were left to the <a href="/wiki/Privateer" title="Privateer">privateers</a> of both sides. Fearing great financial and economic losses should a <a href="/wiki/Spanish_treasure_fleet" title="Spanish treasure fleet">treasure fleet</a> be captured, the Spanish reduced the risk by increasing the number of convoys, thereby reducing their value. They also increased the number of ports they visited and reduced the predictability of their voyages.</p>
<p>In 1744 300 British militia, slaves and regulars with two <a href="/wiki/Privateers" class="mw-redirect" title="Privateers">privateers</a> from <a href="/wiki/Saint_Kitts" title="Saint Kitts">Saint Kitts</a> invaded the French half of neighbouring <a href="/wiki/Saint_Martin" title="Saint Martin">Saint Martin</a>, holding it until the 1748 <a href="/wiki/Treaty_of_Aix-la-Chapelle_(1748)" title="Treaty of Aix-la-Chapelle (1748)">Treaty of Aix-la-Chapelle</a>. In late May 1745 two French royal frigates of 36 and 30 guns respectively under Commodore La Touché, plus three privateers in retaliation sailed from <a href="/wiki/Martinique" title="Martinique">Martinique</a> to invade and capture Anguilla bit were repelled with heavy loss.</p>
<p>The last year of the war saw two significant actions in the Caribbean. A second British <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Santiago_de_Cuba_(1748)" title="Battle of Santiago de Cuba (1748)">assault on Santiago de Cuba</a> which also ended in failure and a naval action which arose from an accidental encounter between two convoys. The <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Havana_(1748)" title="Battle of Havana (1748)">action</a> unfolded in a confused way with each side at once anxious to cover its own trade and to intercept that of the other. Capture was rendered particularly desirable for the British by the fact that the Spanish homeward-bound fleet would be laden with <a href="/wiki/Bullion" title="Bullion">bullion</a> from the American mines. The advantage lay with the British when one Spanish warship ran aground and another was captured but the British commander failed to capitalise and the Spanish fleet took shelter in Havana.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="The_Mediterranean">The Mediterranean</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=War_of_the_Austrian_Succession&amp;action=edit&amp;section=17" title="Edit section: The Mediterranean">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:302px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Combate_de_Tol%C3%B3n.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c0/Combate_de_Tol%C3%B3n.jpg/300px-Combate_de_Tol%C3%B3n.jpg" width="300" height="174" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c0/Combate_de_Tol%C3%B3n.jpg/450px-Combate_de_Tol%C3%B3n.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/c/c0/Combate_de_Tol%C3%B3n.jpg 2x" data-file-width="544" data-file-height="316" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Combate_de_Tol%C3%B3n.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
The Franco-Spanish fleet commanded by Don <a href="/wiki/Juan_Jos%C3%A9_Navarro" class="mw-redirect" title="Juan José Navarro">Juan José Navarro</a> drove off the British fleet under <a href="/wiki/Thomas_Mathews" title="Thomas Mathews">Thomas Mathews</a> near <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Toulon_(1744)" title="Battle of Toulon (1744)">Toulon in 1744</a>.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>While Anson was pursuing his <a href="/wiki/George_Anson%27s_voyage_around_the_world" title="George Anson's voyage around the world">voyage round the world</a>, Spain was mainly intent on the Italian policy of the King. A squadron was fitted out at <a href="/wiki/C%C3%A1diz" title="Cádiz">Cádiz</a> to convey troops to Italy. It was watched by the British admiral <a href="/wiki/Nicholas_Haddock" title="Nicholas Haddock">Nicholas Haddock</a>. When the blockading squadron was forced off by want of provisions, the Spanish admiral Don <a href="/wiki/Juan_Jos%C3%A9_Navarro" class="mw-redirect" title="Juan José Navarro">Juan José Navarro</a> put to sea. He was followed, but when the British force came in sight of him Navarro had been joined by a French squadron under Claude-Elisée de La Bruyère de Court (December 1741). The French admiral announced<sup class="noprint Inline-Template" style="margin-left:0.1em; white-space:nowrap;">[<i>how? <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Please_clarify" title="Wikipedia:Please clarify"><span title="The text near this tag may need clarification or removal of jargon. (October 2010)">clarification needed</span></a></i>]</sup> that he would support the Spaniards if they were attacked and Haddock retired. France and Great Britain were not yet openly at war, but both were engaged in the struggle in Germany—Great Britain as the ally of the Queen of Hungary, Maria Theresa; France as the supporter of the Bavarian claimant of the empire. Navarro and de Court went on to <a href="/wiki/Toulon" title="Toulon">Toulon</a>, where they remained till February 1744. A British fleet watched them, under the command of Admiral <a href="/wiki/Richard_Lestock" title="Richard Lestock">Richard Lestock</a>, till Sir <a href="/wiki/Thomas_Mathews" title="Thomas Mathews">Thomas Mathews</a> was sent out as commander-in-chief and as Minister to the Court of <a href="/wiki/Turin" title="Turin">Turin</a>.</p>
<p>Sporadic manifestations of hostility between the French and British took place in different seas, but avowed war did not begin till the French government issued its declaration of 30 March, to which Great Britain replied on 31 March. This formality had been preceded by French preparations for the invasion of England, and by the <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Toulon,_1744" class="mw-redirect" title="Battle of Toulon, 1744">Battle of Toulon</a> between the British and a Franco-Spanish fleet. On 11 February, a most confused battle was fought, in which the van and centre of the British fleet was engaged with the Spanish rear and centre of the allies. Lestock, who was on the worst possible terms with his superior, took no part in the action. Mathews fought with spirit but in a disorderly way, breaking the formation of his fleet, and showing no power of direction, while Navarro's smaller fleet retained cohesion and fought off the energetic but confused attacks of its larger enemy until the arrival of the French fleet forced the heavily damaged British fleet to withdraw. The Spanish fleet then sailed to Italy where it delivered a fresh army and supplies that had a decisive impact upon the war. The mismanagement of the British fleet in the battle, by arousing deep anger among the people, led to a drastic reform of the British navy.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Northern_waters">Northern waters</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=War_of_the_Austrian_Succession&amp;action=edit&amp;section=18" title="Edit section: Northern waters">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>The French scheme to invade Britain was arranged in combination with the <a href="/wiki/Jacobitism" title="Jacobitism">Jacobite</a> leaders, and soldiers were to be transported from <a href="/wiki/Dunkirk,_France" class="mw-redirect" title="Dunkirk, France">Dunkirk</a>. In February 1744, a French fleet of twenty sail of the line entered the <a href="/wiki/English_Channel" title="English Channel">English Channel</a> under <a href="/wiki/Jacques_Aymar_de_Roquefeuil_et_du_Bousquet" title="Jacques Aymar de Roquefeuil et du Bousquet">Jacques Aymar, comte de Roquefeuil</a>, before the British force under Admiral <a href="/wiki/John_Norris_(Royal_Navy_officer)" title="John Norris (Royal Navy officer)">John Norris</a> was ready to oppose him. But the French force was ill-equipped, the admiral was nervous, his mind dwelt on all the misfortunes which might possibly happen, and the weather was bad. De Roquefeuil came up almost as far as <a href="/wiki/The_Downs" title="The Downs">The Downs</a>, where he learnt that Sir John Norris was at hand with twenty-five sail of the line, and thereupon precipitately retreated. The military expedition prepared at Dunkirk to cross under cover of De Roquefeuil's fleet naturally did not start. The utter weakness of the French at sea, due to long neglect of the fleet and the bankrupt state of the treasury, was shown during the Jacobite rising of 1745, when France made no attempt to profit by the distress of the British government.</p>
<p>The Dutch, having by this time joined Great Britain, made a serious addition to the naval power opposed to France, though the Dutch Republic was compelled by the necessity for maintaining an army in Flanders to play a very subordinate part at sea. Not being stimulated by formidable attack, and having immediate interests both at home and in Germany, the British government was slow to make use of its latest naval strength. Spain, which could do nothing of an offensive character, was almost neglected. During 1745 the <a href="/wiki/New_England" title="New England">New England</a> expedition which took Louisburg (30 April – 16 June) was covered by a British naval force, but little else was accomplished by the naval efforts of any of the belligerents.</p>
<p>In 1746 a British combined naval and military expedition to the coast of France – the first of a long series of similar ventures which in the end were derided as "breaking windows with guineas" – was carried out during August and October. The aim was the capture of the <a href="/wiki/French_East_India_Company" title="French East India Company">French East India Company</a>'s dockyard at <a href="/wiki/Lorient" title="Lorient">Lorient</a>, but it was not attained.</p>
<p>From 1747 until the close of the war in October 1748, the naval policy of the British government, without reaching a high level, was more energetic and coherent. A closer watch was kept on the French coast, and effectual means were taken to intercept communication between France and her American possessions. In the spring information was obtained that an important convoy for the East and West <a href="/wiki/Indies" class="mw-redirect" title="Indies">Indies</a> was to sail from L'Orient. The convoy was intercepted by Anson on 3 May, and in the <a href="/wiki/First_Battle_of_Cape_Finisterre_(1747)" title="First Battle of Cape Finisterre (1747)">first Battle of Cape Finisterre</a>, British admiral George Anson's fourteen ships of the line wiped out the French escort of six ships of the line and three armed Indiamen, although in the meantime the merchant ships escaped.</p>
<p>On 14 October, another French convoy, protected by a strong squadron, was intercepted by a well-appointed and well-directed squadron of superior numbers – the squadrons were respectively eight French and fourteen British – in the <a href="/wiki/Bay_of_Biscay" title="Bay of Biscay">Bay of Biscay</a>. In the <a href="/wiki/Second_Battle_of_Cape_Finisterre_(1747)" title="Second Battle of Cape Finisterre (1747)">second Battle of Cape Finisterre</a> which followed, the French admiral, Henri-François des Herbiers-l'Étenduère, succeeded in covering the escape of most of the merchant ships, but Hawke's British squadron took six of his warships. Most of the merchantmen were later intercepted and captured in the West Indies. This disaster convinced the French government of its helplessness at sea, and it made no further effort.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="The_Indian_Ocean">The Indian Ocean</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=War_of_the_Austrian_Succession&amp;action=edit&amp;section=19" title="Edit section: The Indian Ocean">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/First_Carnatic_War" title="First Carnatic War">First Carnatic War</a></div>
<div role="navigation" class="navbox" aria-labelledby="First_Carnatic_War" style="margin:0;float:right;clear:right;width:315px;margin-bottom:0.5em;margin-left:1em;;padding:3px">
<table class="nowraplinks collapsible autocollapse navbox-inner" style="border-spacing:0;background:transparent;color:inherit">
<tr>
<th scope="col" class="navbox-title" colspan="2" style="background-color:#B0C4DE;">
<div class="plainlinks hlist navbar mini">

<li class="nv-talk"><a href="/wiki/Template_talk:Campaignbox_First_Carnatic_War" title="Template talk:Campaignbox First Carnatic War"><abbr title="Discuss this template" style=";background-color:#B0C4DE;;background:none transparent;border:none;-moz-box-shadow:none;-webkit-box-shadow:none;box-shadow:none;">t</abbr></a></li>
<li class="nv-edit"><a class="external text" href="//en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Template:Campaignbox_First_Carnatic_War&amp;action=edit"><abbr title="Edit this template" style=";background-color:#B0C4DE;;background:none transparent;border:none;-moz-box-shadow:none;-webkit-box-shadow:none;box-shadow:none;">e</abbr></a></li>

<div id="First_Carnatic_War" style="font-size:114%;margin:0 4em"><span style="line-height:1.6em"><a href="/wiki/First_Carnatic_War" title="First Carnatic War"><span class="wrap">First Carnatic War</span></a></span></div>
</th>
</tr>
<tr>
<td colspan="2" class="navbox-list navbox-odd hlist" style="width:100%;padding:0px">
<div style="padding:0em 0.25em">
<ul>
<li><a href="/wiki/Action_of_6_July_1746" title="Action of 6 July 1746">Negapatam</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Madras" title="Battle of Madras">Madras</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Adyar" title="Battle of Adyar">Adyar</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Siege_of_Cuddalore_(1748)" title="Siege of Cuddalore (1748)">Cuddalore</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Siege_of_Pondicherry_(1748)" title="Siege of Pondicherry (1748)">Pondicherry</a></li>
</ul>
</div>
</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<td class="navbox-abovebelow" colspan="2" style="background-color:#DCDCDC;">
<div>Part of the <a class="mw-selflink selflink">War of the Austrian Succession</a></div>
</td>
</tr>
</table>
</div>
<p>In the East Indies, attacks on French commerce by a British squadron under <a href="/wiki/Curtis_Barnett" title="Curtis Barnett">Curtis Barnett</a> in 1745 led to the despatch of a French squadron commanded by <a href="/wiki/Bertrand-Fran%C3%A7ois_Mah%C3%A9_de_La_Bourdonnais" title="Bertrand-François Mahé de La Bourdonnais">Mahé de la Bourdonnais</a>. After <a href="/wiki/Action_of_6_July_1746" title="Action of 6 July 1746">an inconclusive clash</a> off <a href="/wiki/Negapatnam" class="mw-redirect" title="Negapatnam">Negapatnam</a> in July 1746, <a href="/wiki/Edward_Peyton" title="Edward Peyton">Edward Peyton</a>, Barnett's successor, withdrew to Bengal, leaving Bourdonnais unopposed on the <a href="/wiki/Coromandel_Coast" title="Coromandel Coast">Coromandel Coast</a>. He landed troops near <a href="/wiki/Chennai" title="Chennai">Madras</a> and <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Madras" title="Battle of Madras">besieged the port</a> by land and sea, forcing it to surrender on 10 September 1746. In October the French squadron was devastated by a cyclone, losing four ships of the line and suffering heavy damage to four more, and the surviving ships withdrew. French land forces went on to make several attacks on the British settlement at <a href="/wiki/Cuddalore" title="Cuddalore">Cuddalore</a>, but the eventual replacement of the negligent Peyton by <a href="/wiki/Thomas_Griffin_(Royal_Navy_officer)" title="Thomas Griffin (Royal Navy officer)">Thomas Griffin</a> resulted in a return to British naval supremacy which put the French on the defensive. Despite the appearance of another French squadron, the arrival of large-scale British reinforcements under <a href="/wiki/Edward_Boscawen" title="Edward Boscawen">Edward Boscawen</a> (who considered but did not make an attack on <a href="/wiki/Mauritius" title="Mauritius">Île de France</a> on the way) gave the British overwhelming dominance on land and sea, but <a href="/wiki/Siege_of_Pondicherry_(1748)" title="Siege of Pondicherry (1748)">the ensuing siege</a> of <a href="/wiki/Pondich%C3%A9ry" class="mw-redirect" title="Pondichéry">Pondichéry</a> organised by Boscawen was unsuccessful.</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Related_wars">Related wars</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=War_of_the_Austrian_Succession&amp;action=edit&amp;section=20" title="Edit section: Related wars">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<ul>
<li><a href="/wiki/Carnatic_Wars" title="Carnatic Wars">First Carnatic War</a> – Anglo-French rivalry in India often seen as a theatre of the War of the Austrian Succession.</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Russo-Swedish_War_(1741%E2%80%9343)" title="Russo-Swedish War (1741–43)">Russo-Swedish War (1741–43)</a> – Swedish and Russian participation in the War of the Austrian Succession.</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/King_George%27s_War" title="King George's War">King George's War</a> – American participation in the War of the Austrian Succession.</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/War_of_Jenkins%27_Ear" title="War of Jenkins' Ear">War of Jenkins' Ear</a> – Anglo-Spanish war which merged into the War of the Austrian Succession.</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Jacobite_rising_of_1745" title="Jacobite rising of 1745">Jacobite rising of 1745</a> – France provided limited support to Charles Edward Stuart's invasion of Great Britain.</li>
</ul>
